Introduction to Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and Its Place in Hanafi Fiqh
Title page introducing the commentary and edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author, commentator, and significance of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah as a key commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Core Idea
Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah is a classic commentary that unlocks al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, the backbone of Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson introduces the text we will be studying: Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah. Understanding its structure and lineage is essential for navigating the commentary and appreciating its authority in the Hanafi tradition. We will explore the key figures and the role of this work in Hanafi scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
The base text is 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri', a concise manual of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH). This matn is foundational for Hanafi fiqh study.
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is often one of the first texts memorized by Hanafi students.
2
Identify the commentator
The commentary, 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah', was written by Imam Abu Bakr ibn Ali al-Haddad (d. 800 AH?). He provides detailed explanations and proofs for the rulings in the Mukhtasar.
Al-Haddad's commentary is known for its clarity and depth.
3
Recognize the editorial work
The edition in hand was critically edited by Prof. Dr. Sa'id Bakdash. Modern editions ensure accurate transmission of the text and include useful annotations.
Always check the editor's credentials when using published classical works.
4
Understand the significance
Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah is widely used in Hanafi seminaries and study circles. It bridges the concise wording of the matn with comprehensive fiqh reasoning.
The commentary often selects the mufta bihi (operative) opinion within the school.

Commentary
This passage is the title page of the book. It identifies the work as 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah', a commentary on 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. The commentary is by Imam Abu Bakr bin Ali al-Haddad (d. 800 AH?), and this edition is edited by Prof. Dr. Sa'id Bakdash. It is part one of the work. The title page provides essential bibliographic information for the student.

Key Terms
الجوهرة النيرة (Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah): The Luminous Jewel, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Imam al-Haddad.
المختصر (al-Mukhtasar): Refers to the concise manual of Hanafi fiqh by Imam al-Quduri, which is the base text being commented upon.
القدوري (al-Quduri): Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text.
الحداد (al-Haddad): Imam Abu Bakr bin Ali al-Haddad (d. 800 AH?), author of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah commentary.

Checkpoint

A) Al-Quduri wrote both.
B) Al-Quduri wrote the Mukhtasar; al-Haddad wrote the commentary.
C) Al-Haddad wrote the Mukhtasar; al-Quduri wrote the commentary.
D) Sa'id Bakdash wrote both.

Key Takeaway
Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah is a vital commentary that deepens understanding of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, a cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh education.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Introduction to Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira and Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Title page and editor's preface introducing the works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the authors and works celebrated in this front matter and state their significance in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira is the key commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, the foundational Hanafi fiqh text.

This front matter introduces two pillars of Hanafi learning: Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a concise manual of fiqh by Imam al-Quduri, and Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, a detailed commentary by Imam al-Haddad. Understanding the relationship between matn (text) and sharh (commentary) is essential for navigating Hanafi scholarship. This lesson orients you to these works and their authors, setting the stage for serious study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary works
Locate the names of the two books mentioned: Mukhtasar al-Quduri (the base text) and Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira (the commentary). Note that the commentary explains the matn.
The title page clearly states these are the two works.
2
Identify the authors
Find the authors: Ahmad al-Quduri (author of the mukhtasar) and Abu Bakr al-Haddad (author of the sharh). Read their biographical descriptions—note titles like 'al-Imam al-A'zam' for Abu Hanifa and 'al-faqih al-nabt' for al-Quduri.
The preface eulogizes both, highlighting their scholarly rank.
3
Understand the editorial context
Recognize that this is a modern edition by Dr. Sa'id Bakdash. The introduction is not part of the original text but is an editor's preface. Distinguish between the commentator's words and the editor's additions.
The phrase 'تحقيق : الأستاذ الدكتور سائد بكداش' indicates the editor.
4
Grasp the significance in Hanafi tradition
Appreciate that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational text for Hanafi fiqh, often studied as a matn. Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira is a standard commentary used to unpack its rulings.
These works are central to the Hanafi curriculum.

To proceed: Indeed, the book 'Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira' by Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad is a great commentary on the blessed book famously known as 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri', on the jurisprudence of the Greatest Imam Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man, the foundational authority and proof among the Hanafi masters. Commentary
This passage is the front matter of the book, comprising the title page and the investigator's preface. The title page provides bibliographic details: the book is 'Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira', a commentary by Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad on 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' in Hanafi jurisprudence, edited by Dr. Sa'id Bakdash, published in 2015. The investigator's preface begins with the basmalah, hamdalah, and salawat, followed by a description of the two works: 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri (362-428 AH) is a foundational text for the Hanafi school, and 'Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira' by Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad is a significant commentary. The preface eulogizes both authors, highlighting their scholarly stature. This introductory material sets the context for the reader, establishing the authority of the text and its place within the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise manual of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri, widely used as a foundational text.
الجوهرة النيرة (Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira): The commentary by Abu Bakr al-Haddad on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, explained in detail.
الإمام الأعظم (al-Imam al-A'zam): Title for Abu Hanifa, meaning 'the Greatest Imam', the founder of the Hanafi school.
الحنفية (al-Hanafiyyah): The followers of the Hanafi school of law.
مقدمة المحقق (Muqaddimat al-Muhaqqiq): The editor's introduction, written by the modern scholar who verified and published the text.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding the Sources: Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jawhara al-Nayyira
Biographical and methodological introduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and significance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, and explain the relationship between the two works.

Core Idea
Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira is an abridgment of a larger Hanafi commentary that remains essential for beginners and scholars.

This lesson introduces two foundational texts of the Hanafi school: Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a concise manual of fiqh, and its commentary al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. Understanding the authors, the structure, and the purpose of these works is crucial for navigating Hanafi primary sources. The editor's preface provides a window into the scholarly tradition and the value placed on this commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn and its author
State the full name of the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, his birth and death years, and his scholarly reputation.
Al-Quduri (362-428 AH) is a key Hanafi authority.
2
Identify the commentary and its author
State the full name of the author of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, his birth and death years, and his background.
Abu Bakr al-Haddad (720-800 AH) was a Yemeni scholar proficient in many sciences.
3
Understand the relationship between the two works
Explain that al-Jawhara al-Nayyira is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and that it is itself an abridgment of a larger commentary called al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Al-Jawhara is about one-third of the size of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
4
Recognize the scope of the commentary
Note that the commentary includes the full text of the matn, additional fiqh issues, and extensive intra-Hanafi differences.
It discusses differences between Abu Hanifa and his students Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar, and others.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
مقدمة المحقق
الحمد لله الكريم الوهاب، المُعطي بحكمته وفضله من شاء ما شاء، وأفضل الصلاة وأكمل التسليم على سيدنا محمد سيد الرسل والأنبياء، وعلى آله الخيرة الأصفياء، وأصحابه البررة الأتقياء، ورضي الله عن السادة الأئمة الفقهاء، ومَن اقتفى أثرهم إلى يوم الحشر واللقاء، وارضَ معهم بفضلك ورحمتك يا أرحم الراحمين، وبعد:
فإن كتاب: «الجوهرة النيرة»، للإمام أبي بكر الحداد، هو شرح عظيم للكتاب المبارك الشهير بـ «مختصر القدوري»، في فقه الإمام الأعظم أبي حنيفة النعمان، الكتاب العمدة الحجة عند السادة الحنفية، ومؤلفه الإمام البارع الجليل، المُبدعُ النبيل ، الفقيه النَّبْتُ، الحُجَّةُ النظّار، المحدث المحقق المدقق : أبو الحسين أحمد بن محمد القُدوري البغدادي، المولود سنة ٣٦٢هـ ، والمتوفى سنة ٤٢٨هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
أما صاحب الجوهرة النيرة» : فهو الإمام العالم العامل، العابد الورع، الزاهد الواعظ، العلامة المفنّن الفقيه النبيه الحصيف، المفسر المتقن المنيف: أبو بكر بن علي الحداد، من أشهر علماء اليمن السعيد، صاحب المصنفات الجليلة كثرة وإفادة في الفقه الحنفي خاصة، وفي التفسير وغيره من العلوم عامة، بل ممن برع في أنواع كثيرة منها، المولود سنة ۷۲۰ هـ ، والمتوفى سنة ٨٠٠هـ ، رحمه الله تعالى.
و«الجوهرة النيرة كتاب رفيع نفيس، ساطع نوره، متألق في حُسنه، سهل العبارة، قريب المعنى، شَرَحَ فيه مؤلفه كامل نص مختصر القدوري، مع زيادة مسائل فقهية مهمةٍ كثيرة، وفروع منتقاة غالية جمةٍ غزيرة، يحتاجها الطالب المبتدي، والعالم الفقيه المرتوي، بل يسعى إليها كلُّ مَن تصدر للتدريس والإفتاء والإفادة، وأراد حل المشكلات وزيادة. هذا، وقد اختصره مؤلفه من كتابه الآخر، وشرحه الكبير لمختصر القدوري: «السراج الوهاج»، الذي جاء في نحو ألف ورقة، ووقع مختصره «الجوهرة» في نحو ثلثه، أو أزيد بقليل.
وكتاب «الجوهرة النيرة كاسمه، جوهرة فقهية غالية، ودُرَّةٌ حنفية مضيئة عالية، تُنير الدروب، وتُيسّر الخطوب، كتاب مليء غزير بأصول المسائل وفروعها، يُعَدُّ من أعظم شروح القدوري، وأكثرها انتشاراً وتداولاً في حياة مؤلّفه وفيما بعده، أي بعد القرن الثامن الهجري، بل قالوا عنه : كتاب لم يسمح الدهرُ بمثاله، ولم ينسج ناسج على منواله».
وقد أفاض مؤلّفه رحمه الله بذكر الخلاف بين الإمام أبي حنيفة وبين أصحابه أبي يوسف ومحمد وزفر في أغلب المسائل، وفي أحيان أخرى يورد خلاف الحسن بن زياد ومحمد بن شجاع الثلجي، وكذلك فيما بين علماء الحنفية وأئمتهم عامة.
هذا، مع اهتمامه بذكر الروايات عن الإمام أبي حنيفة وغيره، وكذلك
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.
Editor's Introduction
Praise be to Allah, the Generous, the Bestower, who gives by His wisdom and bounty whomever He wills whatever He wills. The best of prayers and complete greetings be upon our master Muhammad, the master of messengers and prophets, and upon his pure chosen family, and his righteous pious companions. May Allah be pleased with the noble imams of jurisprudence, and those who followed their path until the Day of Gathering and Meeting. And bestow with Your favor and mercy upon them, O Most Merciful of the merciful. To proceed:
Indeed, the book "al-Jawhara al-Nayyira" by Imam Abi Bakr al-Haddad is a great commentary on the blessed book famously known as "Mukhtasar al-Quduri" in the fiqh of the Greatest Imam Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man. This book is the main authority and proof among the Hanafi masters. Its author is the excellent, majestic Imam, the noble innovator, the insightful jurist, the proof and examiner, the hadith scholar and accurate verifier: Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri al-Baghdadi, born in 362 AH and died in 428 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
As for the author of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, he is the knowledgeable and acting Imam, the devoted ascetic, the abstinent preacher, the multifaceted scholar, the astute jurist, the judicious exegete, the proficient and lofty interpreter: Abu Bakr ibn Ali al-Haddad, one of the most famous scholars of blessed Yemen, author of many excellent works, numerous and beneficial in Hanafi fiqh specifically, and in tafsir and other sciences in general. Rather, he excelled in many types thereof. He was born in 720 AH and died in 800 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
"Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira" is a lofty, precious book. Its light shines, it is radiant in its beauty, easy in expression, close in meaning. Its author explained the complete text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, along with many important additional fiqh issues and abundant, valuable, selected branches needed by the beginning student and the learned, experienced jurist. Rather, everyone who takes up teaching, giving fatwa, and benefiting, and wants to solve problems and increase in knowledge, seeks it. Indeed, he condensed it from his other work, his large commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri called "al-Siraj al-Wahhaj", which was about a thousand folios. Its summary, al-Jawhara, is about a third of it, or slightly more.
The book al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, as its name suggests, is a precious fiqh jewel and a luminous, elevated Hanafi pearl that illuminates paths and eases difficulties. It is a book full of abundant principles of issues and their branches. It is considered one of the greatest commentaries on al-Quduri, most widespread and circulated during the life of its author and after, i.e., after the eighth century AH. Rather, they said about it: "Time has not permitted its like, and no weaver has woven upon its pattern."
Its author, may Allah have mercy on him, elaborated on the differences between Imam Abu Hanifa and his companions Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar in most issues. At other times, he mentions the difference of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and Muhammad ibn Shuja' al-Thalji, and likewise among Hanafi scholars and their imams generally.
This, along with his attention to mentioning the narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa and others, and likewise
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction to the book 'Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira' by Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad, a commentary on 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' in Hanafi fiqh. The editor begins with the basmalah and hamdalah, then introduces the author of the matn, Imam al-Quduri (362-428 AH), praising his qualifications and his book's status as the primary authority among Hanafis. He then introduces the commentator, Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad (720-800 AH), a renowned scholar from Yemen who excelled in many sciences, especially Hanafi fiqh and tafsir. The editor highlights the value of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira: it is a clear, comprehensive commentary that includes the full text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri along with many additional fiqh issues and branches useful for beginners and experts alike. It is an abridgment of al-Haddad's larger commentary 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj', which was about a thousand folios; al-Jawhara is about a third of that. The editor notes that the book is highly esteemed and widely circulated. Furthermore, al-Haddad extensively discusses the differences of opinion within the Hanafi school, between Abu Hanifa and his prominent students (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar), and occasionally other Hanafi scholars like al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and Muhammad ibn Shuja' al-Thalji. He also pays attention to narrations from Abu Hanifa and others. The passage sets the context for the commentary as a rich source of Hanafi fiqh with detailed intra-school differences.

Key Terms
الجوهرة النيرة (al-Jawhara al-Nayyira): The title of the commentary by Abu Bakr al-Haddad on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, meaning 'The Radiant Jewel'.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh text authored by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (362-428 AH), considered a foundational work in the Hanafi school.
الإمام الأعظم (al-Imam al-A'zam): The Greatest Imam, a reverential title for Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man, the founder of the Hanafi school.
السراج الوهاج (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj): The larger commentary by Abu Bakr al-Haddad on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, from which al-Jawhara al-Nayyira is abridged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira is an abridgment of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, providing a comprehensive yet concise commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri with extensive intra-Hanafi differences.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah: Features and Methodology
Editor's introduction describing book's features

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the features of al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and identify its approach to internal and external ikhtilaf, evidence usage, and the role of the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh commentary that balances evidence, ikhtilaf, and practical fatwa guidance.

Before diving into the rulings, it is essential to understand the tool you are using. Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah is not just a commentary; it is a carefully crafted work that bridges the gap between the beginner student and the advanced jurist. This introduction by the editor highlights key methodological features—how the author handles disagreements, cites evidence, and identifies the relied-upon opinion. Grasping these features will help you navigate the book more effectively and appreciate its value in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his background
Note that the author (Ibn al-Sa'ati) was born in 720 AH and died in 800 AH. He wrote this commentary as an abridgement of his larger work 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj'. Understanding his scholarly stature helps assess the reliability of the text.
The author is a later Hanafi jurist, so his work reflects the mature tradition.
2
Recognize the book's scope and structure
The book covers the complete text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, adding many important fiqh issues, branches, and examples. It is about one-third the size of the original larger commentary, making it accessible yet comprehensive.
The book is praised as 'a precious fiqh jewel' and widely circulated after the 8th century.
3
Analyze the treatment of ikhtilaf
The author extensively discusses disagreements within the Hanafi school (between Abu Hanifa and his students Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar, and others like Hasan ibn Ziyad) and also with other imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad). He often clarifies the mufta bihi, but sometimes leaves it unstated.
This shows the book's role in both recording diversity of opinion and guiding practice.
4
Understand evidence usage
The book cites around 500 Quranic verses and 500 hadiths, with clear indication of their relevance. Deductive reasoning (istidlal) is more concentrated in the first quarter. The author also links branches to fiqh principles and maxims.
This makes the book a medium-level text in terms of proof, suitable for students who have basic grounding.
5
Grasp the concept of mufta bihi and its application
The author identifies the relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi) in many disputed issues, but sometimes omits it. This reflects the evolving nature of tarjih within the Hanafi school.
Knowing when the mufta bihi is stated and when it is not helps you use the book for fatwa and further study.

مقدمة المحقق
وغيره من العلوم عامة، بل ممن برع في أنواع كثيرة منها، المولود سنة ٧٢٠ هـ، والمتوفى سنة ٨٠٠هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
و«الجوهرة النيرة» كتاب رفيع نفيس، ساطع نوره، متألق في حُسنه، سهل العبارة، قريب المعنى، شَرَحَ فيه مؤلفه كامل نص مختصر القدوري، مع زيادة مسائل فقهية مهمةٍ كثيرة، وفروع منتقاة غالية جمةٍ غزيرة، يحتاجها الطالب المبتدي، والعالم الفقيه المرتوي، بل يسعى إليها كلُّ مَن تصدر للتدريس والإفتاء والإفادة، وأراد حل المشكلات وزيادة. هذا، وقد اختصره مؤلفه من كتابه الآخر، وشرحه الكبير لمختصر القدوري: «السراج الوهاج»، الذي جاء في نحو ألف ورقة، ووقع مختصره «الجوهرة» في نحو ثلثه، أو أزيد بقليل.
وكتاب «الجوهرة النيرة» كاسمه، جوهرة فقهية غالية، ودُرَّةٌ حنفية مضيئة عالية، تُنير الدروب، وتُيسّر الخطوب، كتاب مليء غزير بأصول المسائل وفروعها، يُعَدُّ من أعظم شروح القدوري، وأكثرها انتشاراً وتداولاً في حياة مؤلّفه وفيما بعده، أي بعد القرن الثامن الهجري، بل قالوا عنه : كتاب لم يسمح الدهرُ بمثاله، ولم ينسج ناسج على منواله».
وقد أفاض مؤلّفه رحمه الله بذكر الخلاف بين الإمام أبي حنيفة وبين أصحابه أبي يوسف ومحمد وزفر في أغلب المسائل، وفي أحيان أخرى يورد خلاف الحسن بن زياد ومحمد بن شجاع الثلجي، وكذلك فيما بين علماء الحنفية وأئمتهم عامة.
هذا، مع اهتمامه بذكر الروايات عن الإمام أبي حنيفة وغيره، وكذلك بيان المفتى به والراجح في المذهب في كثير من المسائل المختلف فيها، وأحياناً يترك ذكره وبيانه.
كذلك كانت للمؤلف رحمه الله عنايةٌ ببيان خلاف الإمام الشافعي في مواطن كثيرة، وخلاف الإمام مالك ولكن بنسبة أقل، مع ذكر دليلهما ووجه قولهما باختصار، كما يذكر في مرات ليست بكثيرة خلاف الإمام أحمد، وبخاصة في قسم العبادات، وهكذا أحياناً نادرة يذكر الخلاف العالي بين الفقهاء، أو خلاف بعضهم .
أما من ناحية ذكر المؤلّف لأدلة المسائل، وبيان وجهة نظر الأقوال المذكورة: فالكتاب فيه أدلة ليست بالقليلة من الكتاب والسنة لكثير من رؤوس المسائل، وأما الفروع والزيادات التي يأتي بها في شرح مقولة القدوري فإنه يُبيِّن وجهة نظر صاحب كل قول فيها باختصار. ويمتاز المؤلف في الجوهرة النيرة بذكر الأمثلة الموضحة لمسائل الكتاب، الميسرة لفهمها، وخاصة في أبواب البيوع والمعاملات.
وهكذا كثيراً ما يربط الفرع المذكور بضابط فقهي يضم أمثلةً أخرى، أو بقاعدة فقهية تشمل مسائل عديدة ويُمكن القول إنه من الكتب المتوسطة في الاستدلال.
وقد كانت نسبة الاستدلال في الربع الأول من الكتاب أكثر بشكل واضح من بقية الكتاب، وبلغ عدد الآيات الكريمة التي استدل بها المؤلف في الكتاب كله نحو ٥٠٠ آية، وأما الأحاديث المستدل بها فكانت نحو ٥٠٠ حديث أيضاً، مع بيان وجه الدلالة منهما.
Editor's Introduction: And other sciences in general, rather among those who excelled in many types thereof, born in the year 720 AH, and died in the year 800 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. And 'al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah' is a noble, precious book, its light shining, brilliant in its beauty, easy in expression, close in meaning. In it, its author explained the complete text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, with many important additional fiqh issues, and many selected abundant precious branches, needed by the beginner student and the erudite jurist, rather everyone who takes up teaching, issuing fatwas, and benefiting, and who desires to solve problems and increase knowledge. This, and its author abridged it from his other book, his larger commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj', which came to about a thousand folios, and its abridgement 'al-Jawharah' came to about a third of it, or a little more. And the book 'al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah' is, as its name, a precious fiqh jewel, a bright high Hanafi pearl, illuminating paths, facilitating difficulties, a book full and abundant with principles of issues and their branches. It is considered among the greatest commentaries of al-Quduri, and the most widespread and circulated in the life of its author and after him, i.e., after the eighth century Hijri. Rather, they said about it: 'A book the likes of which time has not permitted, and no weaver has woven its like.' And its author, may Allah have mercy on him, extensively mentioned the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifah and his companions Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar in most issues, and at other times he mentions the disagreement of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and Muhammad ibn Shuja' al-Thalji, as well as among the Hanafi scholars and their imams generally. This, along with his attention to mentioning the narrations from Imam Abu Hanifah and others, and also clarifying the mufta bihi and the preferred view in the madhhab in many disputed issues, and sometimes he leaves its mention and clarification. Similarly, the author, may Allah have mercy on him, took care to clarify the disagreement of Imam al-Shafi'i in many places, and the disagreement of Imam Malik but to a lesser extent, along with mentioning their evidence and the aspect of their opinion briefly. He also mentions, not too many times, the disagreement of Imam Ahmad, especially in the section of worship, and thus occasionally he mentions high-level disagreement among jurists, or disagreement of some of them. As for the author's mention of evidence for issues and clarification of the viewpoint of the mentioned opinions: the book contains not a few evidences from the Book and Sunnah for many of the major issues. As for the branches and additions that he brings in explaining the statement of al-Quduri, he briefly explains the viewpoint of the owner of each opinion in them. The author distinguishes himself in al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah by mentioning illustrative examples for the issues of the book, facilitating their understanding, especially in the chapters of sales and transactions. Likewise, he often links the mentioned branch to a fiqh principle that includes other examples, or to a fiqh maxim that covers many issues. It can be said that it is a medium book in terms of deduction. And the proportion of deduction in the first quarter of the book was clearly more than the rest of the book. The number of noble verses that the author used as evidence in the entire book was about 500 verses, and the number of hadiths used as evidence was also about 500, along with clarifying the aspect of indication from them.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction to the work 'al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah', a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Ibn al-Sa'ati. The editor praises the book for its comprehensive coverage, inclusion of additional fiqh issues, and its abridged nature from the larger 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj'. The author, born 720 AH and died 800 AH, is commended for his expertise. The book is noted for its extensive treatment of ikhtilaf (disagreement) within the Hanafi school, including the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar, and others like al-Hasan ibn Ziyad. It also addresses disagreements with other imams, particularly al-Shafi'i, and occasionally Malik and Ahmad, with brief mention of evidence. The author clarifies the mufta bihi (operative opinion) in many cases but sometimes leaves it unstated. The book employs around 500 Quranic verses and 500 hadiths as evidence, with clear indication of their relevance. It is considered a medium-level text in terms of deduction (istidlal), with more extensive evidence in its first quarter. The author often links branches to fiqh principles and provides illustrative examples, especially in sales and transactions. This introduction sets the stage for understanding the methodological approach of the commentary.

Key Terms
الجوهرة النيرة (al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah): The title of the book, meaning 'The Luminous Jewel', a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH).
الخلاف (al-khilaf): Disagreement or difference of opinion among jurists within and outside the Hanafi school.
المفتى به (al-mufta bihi): The relied-upon opinion that is given as a fatwa in the Hanafi school.
السراج الوهاج (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj): The larger commentary by the same author on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, from which al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah was abridged.
الاستدلال (al-istidlal): Deductive reasoning or derivation of rulings from evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah is a comprehensive medium-level Hanafi commentary that combines evidence, internal and external ikhtilaf, and practical fatwa guidance, making it an essential tool for students and muftis.

Introduction and Front Matter

Editor's Introduction: Understanding the Author's Method
Editor's explanation of the author's method in al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of the author’s methodology in al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and explain how he presents preferred opinions and evidences.

Core Idea
Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah pairs preferred Hanafi rulings with evidence from Qur’an and Sunnah.

This passage introduces the methodology of the author of al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, a Hanafi commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The editor explains that the author frequently states the muftā bihi and rājiḥ opinions, and provides evidence from Qur’an and Hadith—about 500 of each. The author also compares views of other Imams, especially al-Shafi‘i, and illustrates rulings with examples. Understanding this methodology helps you navigate the book and appreciate how Hanafi scholars weigh proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book’s purpose and audience
Recognize that al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah is a commentary designed to clarify the Hanafi madhhab’s preferred opinions and provide evidence. The editor highlights the author’s aim to present muftā bihi and rājiḥ rulings for disputed issues.
This is a fiqh commentary, not a primary source.
2
Note the coverage of other madhhabs
The author frequently mentions Imām al-Shāfiʿī’s view, less often Mālik’s, and occasionally Aḥmad’s. Understand that this comparative approach helps a student see the distinctive Hanafi position.
The disagreement is cited briefly with evidence.
3
Analyze the use of primary evidence
The book contains about 500 Qur’anic verses and 500 hadiths as proof. The author explains the aspect of indication (wajh al-dalālah), showing how each text supports the ruling. This is a hallmark of the Hanafi method of istidlal.
Wajh al-dalālah is the precise textual clue that yields the ruling.
4
Recognize the role of examples and legal maxims
The author provides illustrative examples, especially in sales and transactions, and links branches to a legal maxim (qāʿidah) or controlling principle (ḍābiṭ). This aids in applying rulings to new cases.
These maxims are key to understanding Hanafi legal reasoning.
5
Assess the editor’s contribution
The current edition is based on multiple manuscripts, with punctuation, paragraph breaks, and explanations of difficult terms. Understanding this helps you trust the text and use it effectively.
The editor improved readability without altering content.

Editor's Introduction

Statement of the muftā bihi (relied-upon) and the preferred (rājiḥ) in the madhhab in many issues of disagreement, and sometimes he leaves mentioning and clarifying it. Likewise, the author (may Allah have mercy on him) had attention to clarifying the disagreement of Imām al-Shāfiʿī in many places, and the disagreement of Imām Mālik but to a lesser extent, mentioning their evidence and the gist of their position briefly, and he mentions in not many instances the disagreement of Imām Aḥmad, especially in the section of acts of worship, and so in rare instances he mentions the higher disagreement among jurists, or the disagreement of some of them. As for the author's mention of the evidences of issues and clarification of the viewpoint of the mentioned opinions: the book contains not few evidences from the Qur'an and Sunnah for many of the main issues. As for the branches and additions that he brings in his commentary on the saying of al-Qudūrī, he briefly clarifies the viewpoint of the proponent of each opinion. The author in al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah is distinguished by mentioning illustrative examples for the issues of the book, facilitating their understanding, especially in the chapters of sales and transactions. Likewise, he frequently connects the mentioned branch to a fiqh controlling principle that includes other examples, or to a legal maxim that covers numerous issues. It can be said that it is among the moderate books in terms of inference. The proportion of inference in the first quarter of the book was clearly more than the rest of the book. The number of noble verses the author used as evidence throughout the whole book is about 500 verses, while the hadiths used as evidence were about 500 as well, along with explanation of the aspect of indication from both. And in many places in the book, he has wonderful rare inferences, and delightful enjoyable insights in explaining the aspect of indication, that delight the student of knowledge and make him fly with joy without wings. And I have likened this book, due to its abundance of branches and issues, to a great pharmacy full of beneficial medicines and effective drugs, waiting and needing a skilled, sagacious, expert physician to select from it the appropriate effective medicine and apply it with his wisdom and foresight to the questions posed to him and new incidents presented to him, so that it may become a healing balm and a sufficient complete adviser. And Allah destined this book to be printed in more than one edition in the late thirteenth century Hijri in the lands of the Ottoman Sultanate, but without scholarly service to it. Then those editions were photographed as they were, and the book spread and its benefit became widespread, but in its sickly form. Thus when Allah honored me by serving the book of al-ʿAllāmah al-Maydānī's commentary on Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī: 'al-Lubāb fī Sharḥ al-Kitāb', I then aspired to produce 'al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah' in a satisfactory scholarly form as much as possible, my chest expanded, then came Allah's help and facilitation, and He facilitated for me its verification and bringing out this luminous illuminating jewel by establishing the correct text of the book from numerous manuscript copies, and making its text bright by breaking up its phrases and sentences, and distinguishing its issues from one another in a way that clarifies them and eases their understanding, by placing punctuation marks, and explaining the obscure and difficult parts of the text in a manner suitable for the reader of this book, and generously for that purpose.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This is the editor's introduction (muqaddimah al-muḥaqqiq) by Sā’id Bakdāsh. He explains the methodology of the author of al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah (a commentary on Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī). The author often states the muftā bihi (relied-upon ruling) and the rājiḥ (preferred opinion) within the Hanafi school for many disputed issues, though sometimes he omits this. He pays attention to showing the disagreement of Imām al-Shāfiʿī frequently, and Imām Mālik less often, with brief mention of their evidence and viewpoint. He also notes the disagreement of Imām Aḥmad occasionally, especially in ʿibādāt (worship). Rarely, he mentions higher-level disagreements among early jurists. The book contains substantial Qur’anic and hadith evidence for many main issues—about 500 verses and 500 hadiths—and the author explains the aspect of indication (wajh al-dalālah). The author excels at providing illustrative examples to make fiqh issues understandable, especially in the chapters of sales and transactions (buyūʿ wa muʿāmalāt). He often links branches (furūʿ) to a fiqh controlling principle (ḍābiṭ) or a legal maxim (qāʿidah). The editor likens the book to a great pharmacy full of effective medicines, but it needs a skilled jurist to apply the rulings correctly. The editor then explains his own editorial work: he based the text on multiple manuscripts, added punctuation, structured the sentences, explained obscure terms, and distinguished issues for clarity. This passage is front matter describing the book's features and editorial contributions.

Key Terms
المفتى به (al-muftā bihi): The relied-upon ruling in the Hanafi madhhab that is given as fatwa.
الراجح (al-rājiḥ): The preferred or preponderant opinion within the school after weighing evidences.
وجه الدلالة (wajh al-dalālah): The aspect of indication or how a text (Qur'an or hadith) supports a particular ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The author of al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah systematically presents the relied-upon Hanafi rulings with evidence from Qur’an and Sunnah, making it a valuable resource for understanding Hanafi fiqh.

Understanding the Editor’s Introduction to Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah
Editor's introduction: value, problems, and methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key editorial features of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and explain why careful scholarly editing is essential for studying Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A good edition of a classical text is like a skilled physician: it diagnoses errors and prescribes clarity.

This lesson unpacks the editor's introduction to Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The editor describes the book's value, the problems with earlier editions, and his own methodology. Understanding this introduction helps you appreciate the scholarly effort behind the edition and use it effectively in your study of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the book's value
Read how the editor praises the author's rare inferences and compares the book to a pharmacy. This highlights the richness of the commentary.
The pharmacy analogy: the book contains many issues (masa'il) that need a skilled jurist to apply correctly.
2
Identify the editorial problem
Note that earlier editions were printed without scholarly service, leading to typographical errors, omissions, and jumbled content. This explains why a new edition was needed.
The editor calls the old editions 'sickly' (saqimah).
3
List the editorial features
Find the specific improvements: collation of manuscripts, punctuation, distinction of issues, explanation of difficult terms, hadith takhrij, and placement of the matn at the top of the page.
These features make the book clearer and more reliable.
4
Understand the editor's motivation
The editor was inspired by his earlier work on Al-Lubab and aimed to present Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah in a bright, accessible form for students and teachers.
The editor cites hadiths about moderation and seeking guidance.
5
Appreciate the outcome
The new edition is presented as a 'new addition to the Hanafi school' that facilitates understanding of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a text accepted worldwide.
The editor humbly acknowledges human limitations.

وله في مواطن عديدة من الكتاب استدلالات رائعة نادرة، ولفتات بديعة ماتعة في بيان وجه الدلالة، يطرب لها طالب العلم، ويطير بها فَرِحاً مسروراً بغير جناح.
وقد شبَّهت هذا الكتاب بكثرة ما حوى من الفروع والمسائل بصيدلية عظيمة، مليئة بالأدوية النافعة والعقاقير الناجعة وهي تنتظر وتحتاج إلى طبيب فقيه ماهر حاذق يختار منها الدواء الناجع المناسب ليُنزله بحكمته وبعد نظره على ما يُعرَض عليه من أسئلة موجهة إليه، ونوازل جديدة مطروحة عليه ؛ ليعود ذلك عليها بلسماً شافياً، وناصحاً وافياً كافياً.
وقدر الله تعالى لهذا الكتاب أن يُطبع أكثر من طبعة في أواخر القرن الثالث عشر الهجري، في ديار السلطنة العثمانية، ولكن بدون خدمة علمية له، ثم صُورت تلك الطبعات كما هي، وانتشر الكتاب، وعم نفعه وهو على صورته السقيمة التي خرج عليها. وهكذا حين أكرمني الله تعالى بخدمة كتاب العلامة الميداني شرح مختصر القدوري: «اللباب في شرح الكتاب»، تطلعتُ حينها لإخراج «الجوهرة النيرة» بصورةٍ علميةٍ مُرْضِيةٍ بقدر المستطاع، وانشرح صدري ثم جاء عون الله تعالى وتوفيقه، ويسر لي تحقيقه وإظهار هذه الجوهرة المضيئة المنيرة، بإثبات النص الصحيح للكتاب من خلال نُسخ خطية عديدة، وجعل نصه مُشرقاً بتفقير عباراته وجمله، وتمييز مسائله عن بعضها البعض، بما يوضحها، وييسر فهمها، بوضع علامات الترقيم، وشرح غريب النص ومغلقه بما يناسب حال قارئ هذا الكتاب، وكريم
لذلك،
مقدمة المحقق
مستواه العلمي.
هذا مع تخريج الأحاديث الواردة في الكتاب، وبيان درجة كل منها من خلال كلام أهل الشأن في ذلك، وكذلك وضعت مختصر القدوري في أعلى الصفحة مميزاً عن الشرح.
وقد خَلَتْ طبعتي الكتاب القديمتين السقيمتين من كل هذه الخدمات وبخاصة ما يتعلق بالأخطاء المطبعية الفظيعة الكثيرة الواقعة فيهما، والأسقاط العديدة وازدحام مسائل الكتاب وتداخل بعضها ببعض، ونحو هذا مما أخل بالكتاب، وأبعد الاستفادة منه عن كثيرين، ولا يعرفُ هذا إلا مَن عاينه وخَبَرَه، وأسهر الليالي الملاح معه، وكما قالت العرب سابقاً: «وَيْلٌ للشَّجِيِّ من الخَلِي».
وإن في خدمة الجوهرة النيرة وتقديمه بهذه الصورة المشرقة إضافة جديدة للحنفية، وعطاءً سديداً مديداً في الفقه الحنفي، نقدمه لكل من يدرس مختصر القدوري أو يُدرسه، ليكون سبباً وعوناً على تيسير فهم وتفهيم هذا المختصر المبارك الذي كُتب له القبول في مشارق الأرض ومغاربها، وذلك فضل الله يؤتيه من يشاء.
* وقد بذلت جهدي في خدمته وتصحيحه وتقديمه بالشكل الماثل الكتاب
بين يدي القارئ الكريم، وكنتُ أسير في رحلتي الطويلة مع ويمثل نُصبَ عيني قول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «سددوا وقاربوا»، وقوله أيضاً : «يا علي! قُل: اللهم اهدني وسددني».
وما عملي هذا إلا جهد البشر المجبول على الضعف، وخير الناس مَن يَعذر الناس.
He has, in many places of the book, wonderful and rare inferences, and delightful and pleasurable insights in clarifying the aspect of indication, which delight the student of knowledge and cause him to fly joyfully without wings. I have likened this book, due to the abundance of branches and issues it contains, to a great pharmacy full of beneficial medicines and effective drugs, waiting and needing a skilled, discerning, and shrewd physician to select the appropriate effective medicine and apply it with his wisdom and foresight to the questions posed to him and the new incidents presented, so that it becomes a healing balm and a sufficient, complete advisor. Allah Almighty decreed that this book be printed more than once in the late thirteenth century AH in the lands of the Ottoman Sultanate, but without scholarly service. Then those editions were reproduced as they were, and the book spread, and its benefit became widespread while it was in the sickly form it came out in. Thus when Allah honored me to serve the book of Allamah al-Maydani, the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab', I aspired then to produce 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah' in a scientific, satisfactory manner as much as possible. My heart expanded, then came the help and success of Allah Almighty, who facilitated for me its verification and the manifestation of this luminous, bright jewel by establishing the correct text of the book from numerous manuscript copies, making its text bright by dividing its phrases and sentences, distinguishing its issues from one another in a way that clarifies them and facilitates their understanding by placing punctuation marks, and explaining the obscure and dense parts according to the level of the reader of this book. [Page 9] This includes the takhrij of hadiths mentioned in the book, indicating the grade of each according to the experts in that field. I also placed Mukhtasar al-Quduri at the top of the page, distinct from the commentary. The two old, sickly editions were devoid of all these services, especially concerning the many terrible typographical errors in them, the numerous omissions, the crowding of the book's issues and their intermingling, and the like, which detracted from the book and prevented many from benefiting from it. Only one who has examined and experienced it and spent sleepless nights with it knows this, as the Arabs previously said: 'Woe to the afflicted from the carefree.' Indeed, serving Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and presenting it in this bright form is a new addition to the Hanafi school and a sound, extended gift in Hanafi fiqh. We present it to everyone who studies or teaches Mukhtasar al-Quduri, to be a cause and aid in facilitating the understanding and teaching of this blessed summary that has been granted acceptance in the East and West of the earth. This is the bounty of Allah; He gives it to whom He wills. I have exerted my effort in serving it, correcting it, and presenting it in the form before the noble reader. Throughout my long journey with it, I kept before my eyes the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Be moderate and seek closeness,' and his saying: 'O Ali! say: O Allah, guide me and make me steadfast.' My work is only human effort, and the best of people are those who excuse others.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction (muqaddimah al-muhaqqiq) to the book 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah'. The editor begins by praising the author's rare and beautiful inferences throughout the work, likening the book to a comprehensive pharmacy full of beneficial issues (masa'il) that require a skilled jurist (faqih) to apply correctly. He notes that the book was printed in the Ottoman Empire in the late 13th century AH but without any scholarly editing, leading to a 'sickly' text. The editor then describes his own motivation to produce a corrected edition after working on another commentary (Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab by al-Maydani). He explains the editorial methods employed: collating multiple manuscripts, correcting the text, adding punctuation, breaking up phrases for clarity, distinguishing separate issues, and providing explanations for difficult terms. He also mentions adding the hadith takhrij (referencing and grading) and placing the original matn of Mukhtasar al-Quduri at the top of the page for comparison. The editor contrasts this new edition with previous ones, which suffered from typographical errors, omissions, and mixing of topics. He expresses hope that this work will benefit those studying or teaching the Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a widely accepted text in the Hanafi school. Finally, he humbly acknowledges his human limitations and cites hadiths urging moderation and seeking guidance from Allah.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): A reference to the Hanafi jurist Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), author of the famous Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
الجوهرة النيرة (Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah): The title of the commentary being introduced, meaning 'The Luminous Jewel'. It is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by an unnamed author (perhaps the editor's own work).
تخريج الأحاديث (takhrij al-ahadith): The process of tracing hadiths back to their original sources and grading their authenticity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The original matn of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
C) The editor's notes
D) The table of contents

Key Takeaway
The editor's introduction shows that careful scholarly editing is essential for reliable study of classical Hanafi texts.

Editor's Introduction: Appreciating Scholarly Editions in Hanafi Fiqh
Editor describes his work on the book

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recognize the value of critical editions of Hanafi texts and explain the editor's methodology in al-Jawhara al-Nayyira.

Core Idea
A careful edition preserves the text and aids understanding; the editor's work is a service to the Hanafi school.

This lesson introduces the editor's preface of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, a key commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The editor explains his efforts to correct errors, verify hadiths, and present the text clearly. Understanding this helps you appreciate the scholarly work behind reliable fiqh texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's tasks
List the specific improvements the editor made to the book: hadith verification, marking degrees, placing Mukhtasar at the top, correcting typographical errors and omissions.
These tasks are part of 'tahqiq' (scholarly editing).
2
Recognize prophetic guidance
The editor cites two hadiths: 'Be moderate and seek closeness' and 'O Allah, guide me and make me steadfast.' Reflect on how these principles apply to his work.
Moderation (sadad) in editing means avoiding excessive or insufficient correction.
3
Reflect on the editor's attitude
The editor humbly acknowledges human weakness and asks for forgiveness and acceptance. Consider why humility is important in scholarly work.
This reflects the Islamic adab (etiquette) of the scholar.

This is along with the verification of the hadiths mentioned in the book, and clarifying the rank of each based on the statements of the specialists in that field, and I also placed Mukhtasar al-Quduri at the top of the page, distinguishing it from the commentary.
The two old defective editions of the book were devoid of all these services, especially regarding the many terrible typographical errors in them, numerous omissions, crowding of the book's issues, and overlapping of each other, and the like, which impaired the book and prevented many from benefiting from it. So follow my path, for I am weak among you, and my mount among the mounts is limping. O God, You are my goal, and Your pleasure is my desire; You are my support and my help. My success is only from God; upon Him I rely, the best Protector and the best Helper.
I ask God the Almighty for pardon, well-being, and acceptance, and I ask Him, glorified and exalted, to end matters with goodness, to forgive us, our parents, our teachers, our spouses, our children, our loved ones, and everyone with a right upon us, and all Muslims, and to hasten general relief. May God's blessings be upon our master Muhammad and his family and companions.

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction to the book 'al-Jawhara al-Nayyira' (the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri). The editor, Dr. Sa'id Bakdash, explains his methodology in preparing this edition. He notes that he has included scholarly verification of hadiths cited in the book, marked them with their degrees of authenticity, and placed the original text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri at the top of the page to distinguish it from the commentary. He criticizes previous editions for containing numerous typographical errors, omissions, and chaotic arrangement of topics. The editor emphasizes that his work is a valuable addition to Hanafi fiqh and hopes it will facilitate the study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. He cites prophetic traditions urging moderation and seeking guidance, and humbly acknowledges human weakness, asking for forgiveness and acceptance from Allah. The introduction ends with the editor's name and affiliation.

Key Terms
تحقيق (tahqiq): Scholarly editing and verification of a text, including checking hadiths, correcting errors, and providing a clear layout.
تخريج (takhrij): Tracing hadiths back to their original sources and assessing their authenticity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) They were published in the same year as this edition.

Key Takeaway
A good edition of a Hanafi text requires careful hadith verification, error correction, and clear layout to serve students and scholars.

Introduction and Front Matter

Biographical Sources for Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad
Biographical source list for the commentator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate the key biographical sources for Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad, the commentator of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah.

Core Idea
Knowing the sources of a scholar’s biography is essential for verifying the authenticity of his works and teachings.

This passage from the editor's preface lists ten sources containing biographical information on Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad, the author of the commentary Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah. While the editor chose not to reproduce the biography of al-Quduri (the matn author) having already done so elsewhere, he provides this list to guide researchers interested in al-Haddad's life. Understanding how to use such source lists is a foundational skill for students of Hanafi fiqh who wish to assess the authority of texts and their authors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject of the Biography
Determine whose biography is being sourced. Here, it is Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad, the commentator, not al-Quduri.
The editor explicitly states he did not cover al-Quduri.
2
Classify the Types of Sources
Categorize each listed source by genre: historical chronicle (e.g., Al-Uqud al-Lu'lu'iyyah), biographical dictionary (e.g., Taj al-Tarajim), library catalog (e.g., Kashf al-Zunun), etc.
This helps understand the nature and limitations of the information.
3
Evaluate Authority and Relevance
Assess the reliability and relevance of each source based on the author's reputation, date, and purpose. For example, Kashf al-Zunun is a standard reference for book titles.
Some sources like Tabaqat al-Khawas are specialized for scholars.
4
Note Intertextual Dependencies
Identify when one source copies from another, as noted for Al-Aqiq al-Yamani, which took its biography entirely from Tabaqat al-Khawas.
Such dependencies affect the independence of the source.
5
Apply to Your Own Research
Use the list to locate primary biographical material. For instance, if you need al-Haddad's teachers, check Tabaqat al-Khawas first.
This skill transfers to any scholar's biography.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصادر ترجمة صاحب الجوهرة النيرة
لم أترجم هنا للإمام القدوري صاحب المتن؛ مكتفياً بما كتبته عنه مطولاً في مقدمة تحقيقي لكتاب: «اللباب في شرح الكتب»، للعلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني.
وأما مصادر ترجمة الشارح الإمام أبي بكر الحداد صاحب الجوهرة فهي:
١- العقود اللؤلؤية في تاريخ الدولة الرسولية ٢٩٦/٢، للعلامة المؤرخ موفق الدين علي بن الحسن الخزرجي الزبيدي، ت ٨١٢هـ، وقد عاش نيفاً وسبعين سنة.
٢- تاج التراجم، للعلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا، ت ٨٧٩هـ، ص.181.
٣- طبقات الخواص أهل الصدق والإخلاص، للعلامة أحمد بن عبد اللطيف الشرجي الزبيدي، ت ٨٩٣هـ، صاحب: «التجريد مختصر صحيح البخاري»، ص۳۹۱.
٤- العقيق اليماني في وفيات وحوادث المخلاف السليماني، للصمدي عبد الله بن علي بن النعمان، توفي بعد سنة ١٠٦٨هـ، (مخطوط في مجلد ضخم، والترجمة فيه مأخوذة بأكملها من طبقات «الخواص»، ونسوخة منه.
٥- كما توجد ترجمة للمؤلف الإمام الحداد على غلاف نسخة «السراج الوهاج» شرح مختصر القدوري المودعة في مكتبة (المولد) مكة المكرمة، وغالبها مأخوذ من طبقات الخواص»، مع تصرف يسير، ومع زيادات.
٦- البدر الطالع بمحاسن من بعد القرن السابع، للشوكاني محمد بن علي، ت ١٢٥٠هـ، ١٦٦/١.
٧- كشف الظنون، لحاجي خليفة، ت ١٠٦٧هـ، في مواضع عدة عند ذكره لكتب الإمام الحداد.
٨- هدية العارفين للبغدادي إسماعيل باشا ت ١٣٣٩هـ ، ٢٣٥/٢.
٩- الأعلام للزركلي خير الدين، ت ١٣٩٦هـ، ٦٧/٢.
١٠- معجم المؤلفين لعمر رضا كحالة ت ١٤٠٢هـ، ٦٧/٣.
*****
(١) وقد حصلت على ترجمته من مخطوطة للكتاب بمساعي الأخ الكريم الفاضل الدكتور محمد أبو بكر باذيب شكر الله سعيه، وجزاه الله خيراً.
Sources for the biography of the author of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah
I did not translate here for Imam al-Quduri, the author of the matn; being satisfied with what I wrote about him at length in the introduction of my critical edition of the book 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kutub' by the scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani.
As for the sources of the biography of the commentator Imam Abi Bakr al-Haddad, the author of Al-Jawharah, they are:
1- Al-Uqud al-Lu'lu'iyyah fi Tarikh al-Dawlah al-Rasuliyyah 2/296, by the historian scholar Muwaffaq al-Din Ali ibn al-Hasan al-Khazraji al-Zabidi, d. 812 AH, and he lived over seventy years.
2- Taj al-Tarajim, by the scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, d. 879 AH, p. 181.
3- Tabaqat al-Khawas Ahl al-Sidq wa al-Ikhlas, by the scholar Ahmad ibn Abd al-Latif al-Sharji al-Zabidi, d. 893 AH, author of 'Al-Tajrid Mukhtasar Sahih al-Bukhari', p. 391.
4- Al-Aqiq al-Yamani fi Wafayat wa Hawadith al-Mikhlaf al-Sulaymani, by al-Samadi Abd Allah ibn Ali ibn al-Nu'man, died after 1068 AH, (manuscript in a large volume, and the biography in it is taken entirely from Tabaqat al-Khawas, and copied from it.
5- Also there is a biography of the author Imam al-Haddad on the cover of a copy of 'Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri deposited in the Maktabah (al-Mawlid) in Makkah al-Mukarramah, and most of it is taken from Tabaqat al-Khawas, with slight modification and additions.
6- Al-Badr al-Tali' bi-Mahasin min ba'd al-Qarn al-Sabi', by al-Shawkani Muhammad ibn Ali, d. 1250 AH, 1/166.
7- Kashf al-Zunun, by Haji Khalifah, d. 1067 AH, in several places when mentioning the books of Imam al-Haddad.
8- Hadiyyat al-Arifin by al-Baghdadi Ismail Pasha d. 1339 AH, 2/235.
9- Al-A'lam by al-Zirikli Khayr al-Din, d. 1396 AH, 2/67.
10- Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin by Umar Rida Kahhala d. 1402 AH, 3/67.
*****
(1) I have obtained his biography from a manuscript of the book through the efforts of the noble virtuous brother Dr. Muhammad Abu Bakr Badhib, may Allah reward his effort and give him the best reward.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a biographical preface by the editor of the present work, stating the sources he used for the biography of the commentator, Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad, author of 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah'. The editor first clarifies that he did not reproduce the biography of the original author of the matn, Imam al-Quduri, as he had already written extensively about him in his introduction to another book (Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kutub). Then he lists ten sources that contain biographical information on al-Haddad. These sources range from historical works on the Rasulid state to specialized biographical dictionaries. The list includes well-known reference works like Kashf al-Zunun, Al-A'lam, and Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin, as well as more specific works like Tabaqat al-Khawas. The editor also notes that one source (Al-Aqiq al-Yamani) is a manuscript that copied from Tabaqat al-Khawas. Finally, he acknowledges obtaining a manuscript of the book through a colleague. This passage serves as a scholarly apparatus for readers who wish to verify the biography of the commentator.

Key Terms
الجوهرة النيرة (al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah): The title of the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational matn of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri.
ترجمة (tarjama): Biographical entry or source for the life of a person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To present a biography of Imam al-Quduri.
B) To list the sources used for the biography of the commentator al-Haddad.
C) To critique the reliability of the sources mentioned.
D) To provide a summary of the book 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah'.

Key Takeaway
A scholarly preface listing biographical sources demonstrates the importance of verifying an author's life through authoritative references, a skill essential for serious study of Hanafi texts.

The Author's Family and Connections
Listing of the author's lineage and scholarly associates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key figures associated with Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad and explain their significance in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Imam al-Haddad’s family and students connect him to the living tradition of Hanafi scholarship.

This lesson introduces the immediate circle of Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad, the author of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. By understanding his family and contemporaries, you will see how his work is rooted in a chain of learned transmission. These connections are not mere biographical trivia; they help establish the authority and reliability of his fiqh work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mentioned Names
Read the Arabic text and list all proper names: his children, Muhammad ibn Umar, Ahmad al-Shirji, al-Alawi, and al-Siddiq ibn al-Burhan.
These are the only individuals explicitly named; the text notes many others are unrecorded.
2
Determine Relationships
For each name, infer their relationship to Imam al-Haddad: are they his offspring, teachers, students, or peers? The text says his children are 'righteous', and the others are listed as part of his scholarly milieu.
The passage does not specify teacher-student roles for all, but biographical context indicates they were contemporaries or students.
3
Understand the Significance
Reflect on why the biographer included these names. They show that al-Haddad was at the center of a scholarly network, which strengthens the transmission of his works and doctrines.
In Hanafi tradition, knowing a scholar's chain of learning is important for evaluating the reliability of his rulings.

وذِكْرُ سيرته الطيبة العطرة

«كان فقيهاً عالماً كبيراً عابداً ورعاً زاهداً، كثير الاجتهاد في العلم والعمل، متواضعاً، متقللاً في مطعمه ومشربه وملبسه، وجميع أموره،
الورع التام . اهـ
Translation of the author of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira: He has righteous, virtuous offspring who move between the mentioned village and the city of Zabid, following their father's path. 2- The jurist, the knower, Muhammad ibn Umar ibn Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Shuʿban, the imam multifaceted in sciences, died 822 AH. (Y) – Ahmad ibn Abd al-Latif al-Shirji al-Zabidi, father of the author of Tabaqat al-Khawass. 4- The great jurist al-Alawi. The jurist al-Siddiq ibn al-Burhan. And besides these, a great multitude beyond count, but biographical books mention only a few of them. ***** (1) See al-Uqud al-Luʾluʾiyya fi Tarikh al-Dawla al-Rasuliyya 2/296. (2) His biography is in Tabaqat al-Khawass, p. 329. Praise of the scholars upon him, and mention of his good and fragrant biography. Numerous high and precious praises came, showing the station of Imam Sheikh Abu Bakr ibn Ali al-Haddad, and mentioning about his pleasing biography good, fragrant, rare stories that sharpen determination and kindle the fire of desire for knowledge and action. I present here what I have come across from his biographers' books: It came in al-Uqud al-Luʾluʾiyya fi Tarikh al-Dawla al-Rasuliyya by al-Khazraji: 'Abu Bakr al-Haddad was a great, knowledgeable jurist, multifaceted, pious, righteous.' And the scholar Sheikh Ahmad ibn Ahmad ibn Abd al-Latif al-Shirji al-Zabidi said in Tabaqat al-Khawass (2), while translating the people of truth and sincerity, and mentioned among them Abu Bakr al-Haddad: 'He was a great, knowledgeable jurist, a worshipper, pious, ascetic, extremely diligent in knowledge and action, humble, frugal in his food, drink, clothing, and all his affairs, with complete piety.' End.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about Imam Abu Bakr ibn Ali al-Haddad, the author of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. It begins by mentioning his virtuous children who reside between the village and Zabid, following his path. Then it lists some of his notable contemporaries and teachers: Muhammad ibn Umar ibn Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Shuʿban (d. 822 AH), Ahmad ibn Abd al-Latif al-Shirji al-Zabidi (father of the author of Tabaqat al-Khawass), the great jurist al-Alawi, and al-Siddiq ibn al-Burhan, noting that many more are not recorded in biographical works. The passage then shifts to praises of Imam al-Haddad from two sources: al-Uqud al-Luʾluʾiyya by al-Khazraji, describing him as a great, knowledgeable jurist, multifaceted, pious, and righteous; and Tabaqat al-Khawass by al-Shirji, emphasizing his deep knowledge, worship, piety, asceticism, diligence in learning and practice, humility, and frugality in all aspects of life. These commendations establish the high scholarly and spiritual rank of the author, which is important for students to appreciate the authority and reliability of his fiqh work.

Key Terms
الورع (al-waraʿ): Complete piety and scrupulousness; refraining from anything doubtful.
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): Utmost effort and diligence in seeking knowledge and performing acts of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Haddad's family and scholarly network anchor his work within the living Hanafi tradition.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Scholarly Praises and Their Significance
Collection of scholarly commendations for the author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the qualities attributed to Imam al-Haddad and evaluate how these commendations lend authority to his fiqh work.

Core Idea
The piety and learning of a Hanafi jurist reinforce the reliability of his legal rulings.

In this lesson, we examine the glowing tributes paid to Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad by two eminent scholars. These are not mere flattery; they testify to his character and scholarship, which are essential when assessing the authority of his fiqh manual, al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. Understanding this praise helps you appreciate why his work has been studied for centuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Sources of Praise
Locate the two scholars who praise al-Haddad: al-Khazraji in al-Uqud al-Luʾluʾiyya, and al-Shirji in Tabaqat al-Khawass.
Both are respected historians and biographers.
2
Extract the Attributes
From each source, list the adjectives used to describe al-Haddad. For example, 'great jurist', 'knowledgeable', 'pious', 'ascetic', etc.
Pay attention to the order and emphasis.
3
Understand the Legal Relevance
Reflect on how these qualities—especially 'wara' (piety) and 'ijtihad' (diligence)—relate to the reliability of his fiqh rulings. A pious jurist is less likely to err knowingly or lean toward license.
In Hanafi theory, a mufti's integrity and knowledge affect acceptance of his fatwa.
4
Compare the Two Praises
Compare al-Khazraji's concise praise with al-Shirji's detailed one. Both highlight similar core virtues but differ in depth.
Differences show the richness of his character.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad and His Works
Biographical introduction and list of works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six major works of Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad and explain the significance of Al-Jawhara an-Nayyira within the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Imam al-Haddad's six works, especially his two commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, established his authority in Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson introduces you to Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad, the author of Al-Jawhara an-Nayyira, which is the commentary you are studying. Understanding his scholarly background and the range of his works helps you appreciate the authority and place of this text in the Hanafi tradition. We will look at the praise he received, list his major works, and note his death date.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his scholarly context
Read the passage to determine who Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad was, when he lived, and which madhhab he belonged to.
He died in 800 AH and was a Hanafi scholar from Yemen.
2
Recognize the praise from historians
Note the quotes from al-Khazraji and al-Sharji al-Zabidi. They highlight the quality and impact of his works.
External validation adds to the author's credibility.
3
List the six major works
Go through the passage and identify each of the six book titles mentioned. They are listed in sequence.
The list includes a Tafsir, two works on al-Nasafi's texts, a commentary on a Hamiliyya poem, and two commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
4
Focus on the commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Notice that two works are commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: As-Siraj al-Wahhaj (the larger one) and Al-Jawhara an-Nayyira (the present book). This shows the importance of the Mukhtasar in Hanafi studies.
Al-Jawhara an-Nayyira is the book you are reading; it is a middle-level sharh.
5
Note the death date
The passage concludes with his death on Saturday night, 6 Jumada al-Ula 800 AH. This helps place him in history.
Knowing the death date aids in understanding the timeline of Hanafi scholarship.

وكلٌّ مَن عَرَفَه وعَرَفها، ومن ذلك :
ما قاله العلامة المؤرخ الخزرجي في «العقود اللؤلؤية»(۱): وله مصنفات حسنة، وبه تفقه طائفة من أهل زبيد، وانتفع به الطلبة نفعاً عظيماً». اهـ
وقال الإمام الشرجي الزبيدي في «طبقات الخواص»(۲):
وله في مذهب الإمام أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه مصنفات جليلة، لم يصنف أحد من علماء الحنفية في اليمن منذ الإسلام إلى عصرنا مثلها كثرةً وإفادة». اهـ
وقد بلغ حجم مصنفاته في المذهب الحنفي نحو عشرين مجلداً»(۳). وسأذكر فيما يلي أسماء كتبه، وبجانب كل منها حجمه بحسب ما ذكره له مترجموه، ومعلوم أن كلاً منهم يصف النسخة التي اطلع عليها، وإن حجم النُّسَخ الخطية وتباينها أمر ظاهر، بسبب اختلاف الناسخ وقاعدته في النسخ.
وأقدم في ذكر مصنفاته كتابه في تفسير القرآن الكريم، وأؤخر ذِكْرَ شرحيه على مختصر القدوري؛ لأتوسع في الكلام عنهما فيما بعد بشكل خاص، مع نقل نماذج منهما.
وقد بلغ عدد أسماء كتبه ستة كتب ضخمة فخمة كبيرة، كل كتاب منها في مجلدات عدة، وقبل الكلام عنها مفصلاً آتي على ذكر أسمائها هنا مجملةً متتالية؛ ليقف عليها القارئ الكريم جملة واحدة، ثم يأتي تفصيل الكلام عنها :
١- تفسير الحداد.
٢- النور المستنير شرح المنظومة النسفية في الخلافيات، لنجم الدين النسفي عمر بن محمد (ت ٥٣٧هـ).
- سراج الظلام وبدر التمام شرح المنظومة الهاملية (في الفقه الحنفي).
٤- الرحيق المختوم شرح منظومة : قيد الأوابد لما فيه من تأليف الشوارد لنجم الدين النسفي (ت ٥٣٧هـ)، صاحب المنظومة في الخلافيات.
ه السراج الوهاج ، الشرح الكبير لمختصر القدوري .
٦ ـ الجوهرة النيرة ، وهو الكتاب الذي بين أيدينا.
وفاته رحمه الله تعالى :
قضى الإمام أبو بكر الحداد عُمُراً عامراً بالعلم والعمل، والتقرب إلى الله تعالى بأنواع من العبادات والطاعات، مع كل خُلُقٍ حَسَن جميل، حتى كف بصره قبل موته بمدة يسيرة، ثم توفي رحمه الله تعالى ليلة السبت، في اليوم السادس من شهر جمادى الأولى، سنة ثمانمائة (٨٠٠)
And everyone who knew him and knew them (his works), including: What the historian al-Khazraji said in 'Al-Uqood al-Lu'lu'iyya': He has excellent works, and a group of people from Zabid learned fiqh from him, and the students benefited greatly from him. End quote. And Imam al-Sharji al-Zabidi said in 'Tabaqat al-Khawass': He has, in the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, magnificent works; no Hanafi scholar in Yemen from the time of Islam until our era has authored works like them in abundance and benefit. End quote. And the volume of his works in the Hanafi madhhab amounted to about twenty volumes. I will mention below the names of his books, and next to each its size according to what his biographers mentioned, and it is known that each of them describes the copy he saw, and the variation in manuscript sizes is obvious due to the difference of the copyist and his method. And I will present first among his works his book on the interpretation of the Noble Quran, and I will delay the mention of his two commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri to expand on them later in a special section, with quotes. And the number of his book titles reached six massive, magnificent, large books, each in several volumes. Before speaking about them in detail, I will mention their names here in summary sequence so that the noble reader can see them together, then the detailed discussion will come: 1- Tafsir al-Haddad. 2- An-Nur al-Mustanir Sharh al-Manẓuma an-Nasafiyya fi al-Khilafiyyat, by Najm ad-Din an-Nasafi (d. 537 AH). 3- Siraj aẓ-Ẓalam wa Badr at-Tamam Sharh al-Manẓuma al-Hamilia (in Hanafi fiqh). 4- Ar-Rahiq al-Makhtum Sharh Manẓuma: Qayd al-Awabid lima fihi min Ta'lif ash-Shawarid, by Najm ad-Din an-Nasafi (d. 537 AH), author of the Manẓuma on al-Khilafiyyat. 5- As-Siraj al-Wahhaj, the Great Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. 6- Al-Jawhara an-Nayyira, which is the book in our hands. His death, may Allah have mercy on him: Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad spent a life full of knowledge and action, and drawing near to Allah through various acts of worship and obedience, with all good and beautiful character, until his sight became weak a short time before his death, then he died, may Allah have mercy on him, on Saturday night, the 6th of Jumada al-Ula, year eight hundred (800 AH).
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction from the book Al-Jawharah an-Nayyirah, which is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri in Hanafi fiqh. It serves to establish the scholarly authority of the author, Imam Abu Bakr al-Haddad, by quoting historians who praise his works and their impact. It then lists six of his major works, showing the breadth of his scholarship: a Tafsir, two commentaries on works by an-Nasafi (one on divergent issues, one on Hanafi fiqh), a commentary on another manẓuma, and two commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri (the larger one, As-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and the present one, Al-Jawhara an-Nayyira). The passage concludes with the date of his death in 800 AH. This front matter is typical of classical Islamic works, providing the reader with context about the author's credentials and the place of the current work among his writings.

Key Terms
الجوهرة النيرة (Al-Jawhara an-Nayyira): The title of the present book, meaning 'The Sparkling Jewel', a Hanafi fiqh commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational abridgment of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely used as a matn.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding the Scope of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and Its Abridgment
Bibliographic description of two linked works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the relationship between al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawhara al-Nayyira and state their reported volumes according to classical bibliographers.

Core Idea
Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira is a concise version of the larger commentary al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, both by the same author.

This passage introduces two key Hanafi works: al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and its abridgment al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. Knowing the size and relationship of these texts helps you navigate classical Hanafi literature and understand the tradition of abridgment (ikhtisar) – a common practice for making comprehensive works more accessible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two works mentioned
The passage discusses al-Siraj al-Wahhaj (the full commentary) and its mukhtasar (abridgment) called al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. Note that both are by the same author.
Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira is the book in hand; it is a condensed version of the larger sharh.
2
Compare the two source reports on size
Al-Allama Qasim (in Taj al-Tarajim) states al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is eight volumes and its abridgment is four. Hajji Khalifa (Kashf al-Zunun) says the full work is three volumes. Consider possible reasons for the discrepancy – different manuscripts, editions, or counting methods.
Discrepancies in volume counts are common for classical manuscripts; they do not affect the legal content.
3
Understand the purpose of abridgment
The author produced a shorter version of his own commentary. This reflects a pedagogical tradition: a detailed sharh for thorough study and a mukhtasar for quick reference or memorization.
Many Hanafi mutun have multiple shuruh and mukhtasarat at various levels of detail.

The Author's Works: Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira
Describing the author's works and their relationship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relationship between al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, and explain the variation in their reported sizes.

Core Idea
Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira is the abridgement of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, a major Hanafi commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

This passage introduces two key works by the same author: a detailed commentary (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj) and its concise abridgement (al-Jawhara al-Nayyira). Understanding their relationship helps you navigate the Hanafi commentarial tradition and recognize that manuscript variations are common in classical works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Works
Locate the names al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawhara al-Nayyira in the passage. Note that both are by the same author and are connected: one is a full commentary, the other an abridgement.
2
Describe Their Relationship
The passage states that al-Jawhara al-Nayyira is an abridgement (mukhtasar) of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. The original commentary is larger; the abridgement condenses it to four volumes.
The author wrote the longer commentary first, then summarized it.
3
Analyze the Manuscript Variation
Note that scholars differ on the exact number of volumes: some say eight, others three for al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. This reflects different manuscript copies, not a textual dispute.
The Azhar copy has 3871 folios, indicating a substantial work.

The Methodology of the Author in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, the Original of al-Jawhara:
As for the condition of the book al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, its status, and the methodology of its author in it, the author said in his introduction, explaining his work and the methodology he followed: "... This is a book I authored as a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, clarifying its difficulties, explaining its problematic issues, being moderate between brevity and verbosity, balanced between expansion and abridgment. I compiled it with concise expressions and beneficial meanings, easy in approach and leadership, close in meaning and benefit. I made it clear for every needy student, and I named it 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj'. I sought help in that from the Most Merciful, the Compassionate. My success is only from Allah. Upon Him I rely, and He is the Lord of the Mighty Throne. Glory be to You; we have no knowledge except what You have taught us. Indeed, You are the All-Knowing, the Wise." End quote. I say: It is a magnificent great commentary, concerned with mentioning evidences, with discussions that are not lengthy, and it frequently mentions examples for issues to clarify them, remove ambiguity from them, and make them pictured in the reader's mind, with many additional branches over Mukhtasar al-Quduri, which he brings from his wide familiarity with Hanafi books, from lengthy commentaries, books of fatwas, and others. He also mentions the differences of the other three madhhabs in many issues.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological introduction describing the author's works, particularly his commentary al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and its abridgement al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. The author first notes that his work al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text of the Hanafi madhhab. He references other scholars' descriptions of the work's size, indicating variation in the number of volumes (some say eight, others three) due to different manuscript copies. He then quotes his own introduction, where he explains his methodology: he aimed for moderation, neither too brief nor too verbose, using concise words and beneficial meanings, making it accessible to students. The commentary emphasizes that al-Siraj al-Wahhaj includes evidence (adillah), moderate discussions, many examples, and additional branches (furu') beyond the original Mukhtasar, drawn from extensive Hanafi sources. It also mentions differences with other madhhabs. This passage sets the stage for understanding the approach of the book being studied (al-Jawhara al-Nayyira) as an abridgement of this larger work.

Key Terms
السراج الوهاج (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj): The title of the author's larger commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, meaning 'The Blazing Lamp'.
الجوهرة النيرة (al-Jawhara al-Nayyira): The title of the author's abridgement of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, meaning 'The Radiant Jewel'.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely used in the madhhab.

Author's Methodology in Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj
Describing the methodology of the author in writing al-Siraj al-Wahhaj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the key methodological principles of the author in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj as stated in his introduction.

Core Idea
The author aimed for balanced commentary: moderate length, clear evidence, and practical examples.

In his introduction, the author outlines his approach to writing al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. He emphasizes moderation, clarity, and utility. Understanding his methodology helps you appreciate the structure and focus of the commentary, and by extension, its abridgement al-Jawhara al-Nayyira.

Guided Path
1
Extract the Author's Stated Goals
Read the quoted passage from the author's introduction. Identify phrases that describe his intention: 'moderate between brevity and verbosity', 'balanced between expansion and abridgment', 'concise expressions and beneficial meanings'.
2
Identify the Key Features
Beyond the stated goals, the commentary includes: mentioning evidences (adillah), moderate discussions, frequent examples, additional branches (furu'), and references to other madhhabs.
3
Understand the Target Audience
The author says he made it clear 'for every needy student', indicating the commentary is designed for students seeking a clear explanation without excessive detail.
This explains why al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, as an abridgement, is even more concise.
