Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a front matter section listing the sources that the author of al-Jawharah al-Nayrah relied upon in his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It includes works from foundational Hanafi texts, such as al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Jami' al-Kabir by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (both Zahir al-Riwayah), to later commentaries and fatwa collections. The entries typically provide the full title, author, death date, and status (printed or manuscript). This serves as a scholarly apparatus showing the breadth of the author's reference material, ranging from early usul works like Ta'sis al-Nazar by al-Dabusi to later supercommentaries like al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. The list also indicates the author's methodology of incorporating both earlier rulings (mutakaddimun) and later deductions (muta'akhkhirun). The inclusion of works like al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid specifically highlights the evolution of Hanafi fiqh through the identification of new issues not explicitly addressed by the founding imams.

Key Terms
زاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat) that constitute the authoritative source of Hanafi rulings.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare or less widely transmitted rulings, often from transmissions like those of Hasan ibn Ziyad, not part of the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab's textual hierarchy ensures stability: Zahir al-Riwayah is the foundation, later works build upon it.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Sources of a Hanafi Commentary: An Introduction to the Bibliography
Bibliography of sources cited by the author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of sources cited in a classical Hanafi commentary (printed vs. manuscript, matn vs. sharh, fiqh vs. hadith) and explain why source verification is essential for a mufti.

Core Idea
A Hanafi mufti's ruling is only as strong as the chain of texts behind it.

This lesson examines the bibliography (مصادر المؤلف) of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. Though it is not a ruling itself, it reveals the scholarly apparatus that supports the commentary. Understanding how to read such a list is crucial for any student of Hanafi fiqh: it teaches you the hierarchy of sources, the difference between printed and manuscript works, and how later scholars rely on earlier authorities. This list is a key to unlocking the provenance of every ruling in the book.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of each entry
For each source, note whether it is a matn (foundational text), a sharh (commentary), a collection of fatawa, or a language/ḥadīth work. For example, al-Jāmiʿ al-Kabīr is a matn by al-Shaybānī, while al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj is a sharḥ.
The author marks printed works with (ط) and manuscripts with (خ).
2
Note the author and death date
Each entry gives the author's full name and ḥijrī death date. This allows you to place the work chronologically and assess its authority in the Hanafi school.
Earlier authors like al-Shaybānī (d. 189) carry greater weight than later ones.
3
Recognize uncertainties
The author sometimes adds question marks or ambiguous phrases like 'perhaps it is...' or 'there is more than one...'. This shows scholarly caution in attribution.
E.g., entry 22 on al-Khujandī: the author guesses it might be al-Kākī.
4
Understand the range of disciplines
The list includes not only fiqh but also ḥadīth (Sunan Abī Dāwūd), sīrah (al-Shifā), and language works (Ṣiḥāḥ al-Jawharī). This reflects the comprehensive training of a Ḥanafī jurist.
Cross-sectarian sources are cited for evidence, not for fiqh rulings.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a front matter section listing the sources used by the author of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. It is a bibliography of Hanafi fiqh works and related texts. The author enumerates 40 titles (from 17 to 40, with earlier numbers presumably in preceding pages). Each entry typically gives the short title, the full name of the author, death date, and often a note on whether it is printed (ط) or manuscript (خ). Some entries include remarks about uncertainty or multiple possible identifications. This section demonstrates the depth of the author's reliance on earlier Hanafi authorities, including foundational works like al-Jami' al-Kabir by Muhammad al-Shaybani, and later commentaries such as the various shuruh on al-Quduri and al-Hidaya. The presence of works by non-Hanafi authors (e.g., Sunan Abi Dawud, al-Shifa by Qadi 'Iyad) shows cross-sectarian citation. The author also notes works he has not seen (e.g., Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by his teacher) and ambiguous references (e.g., al-Hawashi, al-'Uyun). This list serves as a key for scholars to trace the provenance of the rulings cited in the commentary.

Key Terms
مصادر المؤلف (masadir al-mu'allif): The list of sources that the author of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira relied upon in his commentary.
الجامع الكبير (al-Jami' al-Kabir): A major Hanafi fiqh compilation by Muhammad al-Shaybani, part of the Zahir al-Riwayah.
السنن (al-Sunan): The hadith collection of Abu Dawud, one of the six canonical hadith books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Knowing the sources and their authority is essential for a Hanafi mufti to issue reliable fatwas.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
The Hanafi Bibliographical Tradition: Sources in al-Jawhara al-Nayyira
List of works cited by the author, showing the breadth of Hanafi literature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi fiqh works listed in the author's bibliography and classify each by genre (e.g., matn, sharh, fatwa collection).

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar's bibliography reveals the layered authority of the madhhab: from early compendia to later fatwa collections.

This lesson explores the bibliography of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The author lists dozens of works he consulted, ranging from the foundational texts of Imam Muhammad to later fatwa compilations. Understanding these sources is key to navigating the Hanafi textual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Scan the list for variety of genres
Look for terms like 'مبسوط', 'مختصر', 'فتاوى', 'شرح' to identify matn, sharh, fatwa collections.
Many works have multiple editions; note the (خ) manuscript and (ط) print indicators.
2
Identify Zahir al-Riwayah core works
Locate works like al-Mabsut and al-Mujarrad that belong to the six core books of Imam Muhammad.
These are the most authoritative for deriving rulings.
3
Distinguish primary from secondary sources
Primary sources are direct transmissions or early compilations (e.g., al-Mujarrad); secondary are commentaries or later summaries (e.g., Kanz al-Daqa'iq).
This hierarchy affects legal weight.
4
Note the role of fatwa collections
Works like Fatawa Qadi Khan and al-Fatawa al-Sughra represent later juristic practice and are used for fatwa.
They are not part of Zahir al-Riwayah but are essential for applied fiqh.
5
Recognize the author's method
The author cites both manuscripts and printed editions, showing his scholarly thoroughness.
This list is selective; not all Hanafi works are included.

Commentary
This is a bibliography section from the introduction of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. The author lists the primary and secondary sources he relied upon in his commentary. The list includes fatwa collections (al-Fatawa al-Sughra, al-Fatawa al-Kubra, Fatawa Qadi Khan, etc.), major Hanafi works (al-Mabsut, al-Mujarrad, al-Muhit, Kanz al-Daqa'iq), commentaries (Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, al-Mustasfa), and others. The notations (خ) for manuscript and (ط) for print indicate the availability of these works. Many of these works are foundational to the Hanafi madhhab, such as al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi, which is a comprehensive commentary on al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid. The mention of 'al-Karkhi' refers to the works of al-Karkhi, a major Hanafi jurist. The author also references tafsir works like al-Kashshaf by al-Zamakhshari. This list demonstrates the depth of the author's scholarship and the rich tradition of Hanafi fiqh literature.

Key Terms
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): A major Hanafi fiqh work by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, being a commentary on al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid.
الفَتاوىٰ (al-Fatawa): Compilations of legal opinions (fatwas) by various Hanafi scholars, often named after the author.
المجرد لأبي حنيفة (al-Mujarrad li Abi Hanifa): A compilation of rulings directly transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa by his student al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i.
فتاوى قاضي خان (Fatawa Qadi Khan): A collection of fatwas by Qadi Khan (Hasan ibn Mansur al-Uzjandi), a major Hanafi jurist.
كنز الدقائق (Kanz al-Daqa'iq): A later matn (textbook) by al-Nasafi, summarizing Hanafi rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a direct transmission from Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) al-Mabsut
B) al-Mujarrad
C) Kanz al-Daqa'iq
D) al-Fatawa al-Sughra

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi work's position in the madhhab is determined by its genre and date; commentaries on earlier texts (shuruh) and direct transmissions (like al-Mujarrad) are the most authoritative.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Hanafi Fiqh Library: An Overview of Classical Sources
Lists classical Hanafi texts by genre.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the listed Hanafi works into the genres of matn (concise text), sharh (commentary), fatwa collection, and nawadir (rare transmissions).

Core Idea
The Hanafi school preserved rulings through a layered literary tradition—from concise matns to comprehensive commentaries and fatwa compilations.

In this lesson, we explore the rich bibliography of classical Hanafi sources that the author of الجوهرة النيرة relied upon. By understanding the different genres—matn, sharh, fatwa collections, and nawadir—you will learn how the school transmitted rulings across centuries. This overview will help you later assess the authority of each text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matns (concise primary texts)
Look for works that are short, original summaries of fiqh, such as Kanz al-Daqaiq (entry 54) and Mukhtasar al-Karkhi (entry 58). These are the foundations upon which commentaries were built.
Matns are typically memorized by students.
2
Identify the shuruh (commentaries)
Commentaries expand on matns. Examples include Al-Mabsut (55) on al-Kafi, Al-Hidayah (74) on Bidayat al-Mubtadi, and Al-Nihaya (70) on Al-Hidayah. Note the chain: matn → sharh → super-commentary.
Al-Hidayah is among the most influential Hanafi commentaries.
3
Identify fatwa collections and nawadir
Fatwa collections gather rulings from multiple authorities, e.g., Al-Multaqat fi al-Fatawa (66) and Al-Nawazil (73). Nawadir contain non-standard transmissions, e.g., Al-Nawadir (71) and Al-Mujarrad (56).
Nawadir are less authoritative than zahir al-riwayah works.
4
Note the presence of manuscripts vs. prints
Entries marked (خ) are manuscripts, (ط) are printed. This shows the historical availability of texts. For instance, Al-Muhit (57) exists in both manuscript and print editions.
Manuscripts may contain variants; printed editions are more standardized.

مصادر المؤلف
٥٤ كنز الدقائق، للنسفي أبي البركات عبدالله بن أحمد، ت ۷۱۰هـ ، (ط).
٥٥- المبسوط، (شرح الكافي للحاكم الشهيد)، لشمس الأئمة السرخسي أبي بكر محمد بن أحمد ، ت ٤٨٣هـ، وقيل٤٩٠هـ، (ط).
٥٦ـ المجرد لأبي حنيفة، للحسن بن زياد اللؤلؤي تلميذ الإمام أبي حنيفة، ت٢٠٤هـ، (ط).
٥٧ المحيط، لمحمد بن محمد بن الإسلام السرخسي، ت ٥٧١هـ، (خ). وهناك المحيط، لبرهان الدين محمود بن تاج الدين أحمد ابن الصدر الشهيد برهان الأئمة عبد العزيز بن عمر البخاري، ت ٦١٦هـ، وهو ابن أخي الصدر الشهيد، (ط). وهناك محيط السرخسي، لشمس الأئمة محمد بن أحمد، ت ٤٨٣ هـ، (خ).
٥٨ـ مختصر الكرخي، عبيد الله بن الحسين الكرخي، ت٣٤٠هـ، (خ).
٥٩- المرتبة ؟ .
٦٠ـ المستصفى (شرح منظومة النسفي في الخلاف، للنسفي أبي حفص عمر بن محمد، ت ٥٣٧هـ)، للنسفي أبي البركات عبد الله بن أحمد، ت ٧١٠هـ، (خ).
٦١ ـ المشكل. هكذا مطلقاً، وهناك أكثر من كتاب بهذا الاسم.
٦٢ـ مشكل القدوري.
٦٣ ـ المصابيح. هناك أكثر من كتاب بهذا الاسم.
٦٤ - المصفى مختصر المستصفى للنسفي = المستصفى.
٦٥- المغرب في ترتيب المعرب، للمطرزي ناصر الدين بن عبد السيد، ت ٦١٠هـ، (ط).
٦٦ - الملتقط في الفتاوى، لأبي القاسم بن يوسف السمرقندي، ت ٥٥٦هـ ، (ط).
٦٧ـ المنتقى. هناك أكثر من منتقى.
٦٨ - المنظومة في الخلافيات، لعمر بن محمد نجم الدين النسفي، ت ٥٣٧هـ، (ط).
٦٩ - منية المصلي وغنية المبتدي للكاشغري محمد بن محمد، ت ٧٠٥هـ، (ط).
٧٠ النهاية شرح الهداية، للسغناقي الحسين بن علي، ت ٧١٠هـ، (خ)، وهو تلميذ صاحب الهداية والنهاية أول شرح للهداية. ينظر كشف الظنون ٢٠٣٢/٢.
۷۱ - النوادر، لمحمد بن الحسن الشيباني، ت ١٨٩هـ، (خ)، له عدة روايات منها لابن سماعة، ت ٢٣٣هـ، ومنها: لهشام بن عبيد الله الرازي، ت ٢٢١هـ، ومنها : لابن رُسْتُم إبراهيم، ت ٢١١هـ.
۷۲ نوادر بشر عن أبي يوسف، بشر بن الوليد الكندي، ت٢٣٨هـ.
٧٣- النوازل. لعله لأبي الليث السمرقندي نصر بن محمد، ت ۳۷۳هـ.
٧٤- الهداية شرح بداية المبتدي للمرغيناني علي بن أبي بكر، ت ٥٩٣هـ ، (ط).
٧٥- الواقعات للصدر الشهيد عمر بن عبد العزيز بن مازه.

And there is Muhit al-Sarakhsi, by Shams al-A'imma Muhammad ibn Ahmad, d. 483 H, (manuscript).

59- Al-Murattabah? [uncertain].
60- Al-Mustasfa (commentary on the versified work of al-Nasafi on legal disagreements, by al-Nasafi Abu Hafs Umar ibn Muhammad, d. 537 H), by al-Nasafi Abu al-Barakat Abd Allah ibn Ahmad, d. 710 H, (manuscript).

62- Mushkil al-Quduri.
63- Al-Masabih. There is more than one book with this name.

65- Al-Mughrib fi Tartib al-Mu'rib, by al-Mutarrizi Nasir al-Din ibn Abd al-Sayyid, d. 610 H, (print).
66- Al-Multaqat fi al-Fatawa, by Abu al-Qasim ibn Yusuf al-Samarqandi, d. 556 H, (print).

69- Munyat al-Musalli wa Ghunyat al-Mubtadi, by al-Kashghari Muhammad ibn Muhammad, d. 705 H, (print).
70- Al-Nihaya: commentary on al-Hidaya, by al-Sighnaqi al-Husayn ibn Ali, d. 710 H, (manuscript), and he is a student of the author of al-Hidaya, and al-Nihaya is the first commentary on al-Hidaya. See Kashf al-Zunun 2/2032.
71- Al-Nawadir, by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, d. 189 H, (manuscript). It has several transmissions: one from Ibn Sama'a, d. 233 H; another from Hisham ibn Ubayd Allah al-Razi, d. 221 H; another from Ibn Rustum Ibrahim, d. 211 H.
72- Nawadir Bishr from Abu Yusuf, by Bishr ibn al-Walid al-Kindi, d. 238 H.
73- Al-Nawazil. Perhaps by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi Nasr ibn Muhammad, d. 373 H.
74- Al-Hidaya: commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi, by al-Marghinani Ali ibn Abi Bakr, d. 593 H, (print).
75- Al-Waqi'at, by al-Sadr al-Shahid Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Mazah.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography (مصادر المؤلف) listing the classical Hanafi works that the author of الجوهرة النيرة used as sources. It demonstrates the breadth of the Hanafi tradition, ranging from early foundational works like Al-Mujarrad by Hasan ibn Ziyad (a direct student of Abu Hanifa) and Al-Nawadir by Muhammad al-Shaybani, to later commentaries like Al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi and Al-Hidaya of al-Marghinani. The list includes both printed editions (ط) and manuscripts (خ), reflecting the state of availability. Notable works: Kanz al-Daqaiq is a concise Hanafi fiqh text; Al-Mabsut is a comprehensive commentary; Al-Hidaya is a central reference; Al-Nawadir contains rare transmissions from Imam Muhammad. The author also references collections of fatawa (Al-Multaqat, al-Nawazil) and works on legal disagreement (Al-Manzuma fi al-Khilafiyyat). This list is typical of later Hanafi works, showing the cumulative scholarly tradition.

Key Terms
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): A comprehensive commentary by al-Sarakhsi on al-Kafi of al-Hakim al-Shahid, a major source of Hanafi fatwa.
الهداية (al-Hidayah): A commentary by al-Marghinani on his own Bidayat al-Mubtadi, a standard Hanafi fiqh manual.
النوادر (al-Nawadir): A collection of rare transmissions from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, containing views not in the zahir al-riwayah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school produced a rich literary tradition of matns, commentaries, fatwa collections, and nawadir, each with a distinct role and level of authority.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Authority Levels in the Hanafi School: Distinguishing Zahir al-Riwayah from Nawadir
Highlights authority levels among listed sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between zahir al-riwayah works (like al-Mabsut) and nawadir (like al-Nawadir) and explain their different authority in Hanafi fatwa.

Core Idea
Not all Hanafi texts carry equal weight—later fatwa relies on the authoritative zahir al-riwayah, not on rare nawadir transmissions.

In the Hanafi textual tradition, some works are considered the standard reference (zahir al-riwayah), while others contain rare opinions (nawadir). This lesson uses the bibliography from الجوهرة النيرة to help you identify these categories. Understanding the hierarchy is crucial for any student of fiqh, as it directly impacts which ruling is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the zahir al-riwayah works in the list
Zahir al-riwayah refers to the six books compiled by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat. While not all six are listed, al-Mabsut (55) is a commentary on al-Kafi (which is based on zahir al-riwayah). Also, al-Hidayah (74) is a commentary that systematizes the school's relied-upon views.
Al-Mabsut is a comprehensive commentary that consolidates zahir al-riwayah.
2
Identify the nawadir works
Nawadir contain transmissions outside the six books. Clear examples are al-Nawadir (71) by Muhammad al-Shaybani himself, and al-Mujarrad (56) by Hasan ibn Ziyad. Note that al-Nawadir has multiple chains of transmission (riwayah) as recorded in the passage.
Nawadir are valuable for study but not primary for fatwa.
3
Understand why nawadir are less authoritative
The Hanafi school gives precedence to the views transmitted through the six books (zahir al-riwayah) because they were most widely accepted and transmitted. Nawadir may contain opinions that were later abandoned or contradicted by the majority of the school. Hence, muftis typically stick to the zahir al-riwayah.
This does not mean nawadir are incorrect—only that they are not the basis for fatwa.

This passage is a bibliography (مصادر المؤلف) listing the classical Hanafi works that the author of الجوهرة النيرة used as sources. Notable works: Kanz al-Daqaiq is a concise Hanafi fiqh text; Al-Mabsut is a comprehensive commentary; Al-Hidaya is a central reference; Al-Nawadir contains rare transmissions from Imam Muhammad. ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad that form the standard compilation of the school's major positions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the authoritative zahir al-riwayah (e.g., al-Mabsut, al-Hidayah) and the rare nawadir (e.g., al-Nawadir, al-Mujarrad); fatwa is based on the former.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Hanafi Scholarly Tradition: Sources of Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira
List of works cited by the author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi legal sources cited by al-Marghinani and classify them by type (commentary, fatwa collection, nawadir, etc.).

Core Idea
A bibliography reveals the chain of authority: from al-Hidaya to rare transmissions in al-Nawadir.

This passage lists the works that the author of Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira relied upon. Understanding these sources helps you appreciate the depth and hierarchy of Hanafi legal literature. Each work has a distinct role and authority level. Let's walk through the list to see how they fit together.

Guided Path
1
Identify each source entry
For each numbered entry (64–78), note the title, author, death date, and whether it is printed (ط) or manuscript (خ).
Some entries like 'al-Muntaqa' are ambiguous; there may be multiple works with the same name.
2
Classify by genre
Determine whether each work is a matn (base text), sharh (commentary), nawadir (rare transmissions), fatawa/nawazil (fatwa collection), or other (e.g., lexical work).
For example, 'al-Nawadir' is a collection of rare transmissions, while 'al-Hidaya' is a commentary.
3
Note the authority level
Identify which works belong to Zahir al-Riwayah (core texts) and which are nawadir (less authoritative). Also note if the work is a first commentary or a later compilation.
Al-Hidaya is a Zahir al-Riwayah text; al-Nawadir has lower authority.
4
Trace connections between works
Look for relationships: al-Nihaya is the first commentary on al-Hidaya; al-Yanabi' is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri (the matn of Al-Jawhara).
Understanding these connections helps you see the chain of transmission.
5
Assess the scope of the list
Notice that the list includes both early authorities (Muhammad al-Shaybani, d. 189) and later scholars (al-Sighnaqi, d. 710). This shows the chronological range of sources.
The author draws from over 500 years of Hanafi scholarship.

Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This is a bibliography (مصادر المؤلف) listing the sources used by the author of Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. The list numbers sources from 64 to 78, indicating that earlier portions (not shown) included entries 1–63. The author draws on a wide range of Hanafi legal works: commentaries, fatwa collections, and secondary compilations. Notable entries include: Al-Nihaya Sharh al-Hidaya by al-Sighnaqi, the first commentary on al-Marghinani's Al-Hidaya; Al-Nawadir by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani with multiple transmission chains; and Al-Yanabi' Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Rashid al-Din al-Rumi, a direct commentary on the matn of the present work. The list includes both printed (ط) and manuscript (خ) sources. This passage serves as a front matter reference, showing the scholarly tradition that the author relied upon.

Key Terms
الهداية (al-Hidaya): A foundational Hanafi fiqh work by al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH), commentary on his own Bidayat al-Mubtadi.
النوادر (al-Nawadir): A collection of rare transmissions (nawadir) from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, containing rulings not in the Zahir al-Riwayah.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh manual by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), the base text of Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira.

Key Takeaway
The sources cited in Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira span matn, sharh, nawadir, and fatawa, forming a comprehensive picture of Hanafi legal literature.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Manuscript Basis of a Critical Edition - Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah
Introduction describing manuscript copies used in the critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key criteria used by editors to evaluate manuscript copies of Hanafi fiqh texts and explain how these criteria affect the reliability of the critical edition.

Core Idea
A critical edition's trustworthiness depends on the age, completeness, and accuracy of its manuscript witnesses.

This lesson examines the manuscript foundation of the critical edition of al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, a Hanafi fiqh commentary. The editor describes fourteen copies with varying dates, features, and locations. Understanding how these manuscripts were selected and described helps us gauge the reliability of the published text.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the role of manuscript witnesses
Understand that a critical edition reconstructs a text from handwritten copies. The quality of these copies directly impacts the accuracy of the edited text.
Manuscripts are the primary source for pre-print era texts.
2
Analyze the provided manuscript descriptions
Examine each copy's date, folio count, lines per page, presence of vowelization, corrections, and location. These details indicate the copyist's care and the manuscript's lineage.
Older copies are generally more reliable, but corrections and completeness also matter.
3
Compare features across copies
Note differences such as vowelization (dabt) from beginning or partially, marginal notes, and distinguishing marks. These features help assess each copy's usefulness for establishing the text.
For example, the 1031 AH copy has vowelization and a line separating al-Quduri from the commentary.
4
Evaluate overall reliability
Consider how the editor's choice of these fourteen copies (out of many) affects the resulting edition. A diversity of witnesses from different periods and regions strengthens the text.
The editor states there are about a hundred copies worldwide; his selection covers a range of dates and provenance.

The Manuscript Copies Used in the Critical Edition of Al-Jawharah Al-Nayyirah. Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah has many manuscript copies in world libraries; see the comprehensive index, which mentions 161 pieces of al-Jawharah, i.e., about a hundred copies. There are also many other copies of the book in world libraries not mentioned in this index. Allah facilitated for me obtaining images of fourteen copies, and below is a summary description of them, arranged according to the antiquity of their copying dates: 1- A copy dated 950 AH, consisting of 290 folios, each page having 35 lines, and the quotations are in red ink. The original of this copy is preserved in the Köprülü Library in Istanbul, and an image of it was sent to me by Brother Dr. Ilyas Qablan, may Allah reward him. 2- A copy dated 974 AH, consisting of 313 folios, each page having 35 lines, with little vowelization, some marginal notes, ordinary handwriting, the text of al-Jawharah is mostly correct, complete, and without omissions. I obtained an image of it from the King Faisal Center for Research and Islamic Studies in Riyadh. 3- A copy dated 977 AH, consisting of 400 folios, each page having 23 lines, each line 11 words, excellent, with beautiful clear handwriting, rare vowelization, photographed from the library of Sheikh al-Islam Feyzullah Efendi in Istanbul, and a copy of it is in the King Abdullah bin Abdulaziz Library at Umm al-Qura University. 4- A copy also dated 977 AH, consisting of 364 folios, each page having 33 lines, each line 12 words, fairly excellent, with beautiful clear handwriting, no vowelization, an image of it is in the Juma Al-Majid Center in Dubai, and its original is in the Gazi Husrev Library in Turkey. It appears that its owner had a clear engagement with it, many revisions, placed some beneficial marginal notes and comments, corrections to its text, and in its margins are headings that highlight the content of the book. 5- A copy dated 1031 AH, consisting of 345 folios, each page having 33 lines, with excellent vowelization for many words, a line placed on the text of al-Quduri to distinguish it from al-Jawharah, verification and comparison with the text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. An image of this copy is deposited at Umm al-Qura University in Makkah. 6- A copy dated 1041 AH, consisting of 314 folios, each page having 31 lines, each line 16 words, fairly excellent, with beautiful clear handwriting, vowelization from the beginning to folio 55 only, photographed from the library of Sheikh al-Islam Feyzullah Efendi in Istanbul, and an image of it is in the King Abdullah bin Abdulaziz Library at Umm al-Qura University. - A copy dated 1058 AH, in two parts, the first with number 124, ...
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is front matter from the critical edition of al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, describing the manuscript copies used by the editor. The author states that there are many manuscript copies worldwide — the comprehensive index lists 161 pieces for al-Jawharah, approximately a hundred complete copies. He obtained images of fourteen copies. He then lists six copies in detail, ordered by date: 1) 950 AH (Köprülü, Istanbul) — 290 folios, 35 lines/page, red ink for quotations. 2) 974 AH (King Faisal Center, Riyadh) — 313 folios, 35 lines/page, mostly correct text. 3) 977 AH (Feyzullah Efendi, Istanbul) — 400 folios, 23 lines/page, 11 words/line, excellent quality. 4) Another 977 AH (Gazi Husrev, Turkey) — 364 folios, 33 lines/page, 12 words/line, with marginal notes and corrections. 5) 1031 AH (Umm al-Qura, Makkah) — 345 folios, 33 lines/page, with line distinguishing al-Quduri from al-Jawharah. 6) 1041 AH (Feyzullah Efendi, Istanbul) — 314 folios, 31 lines/page, vowelization only up to folio 55. The editor also mentions a 1058 AH copy in two parts. This description is typical in scholarly editions to establish the authority of the text.

Key Terms
نسخة خطية (nuskhah khattiyyah): A handwritten manuscript copy of a book.
الفهرس الشامل (al-fihris al-shamil): The comprehensive index of Arabic manuscripts, likely referring to a published catalog.
ضبط (dabt): Vowelization and diacritical marks added to the Arabic text to ensure correct pronunciation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The critical edition's text is only as reliable as the manuscript copies upon which it is based.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Role of Manuscript Copies in Hanafi Textual Transmission
Bibliographic list of approved manuscripts for a critical edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why manuscript verification is essential for establishing the authentic text of a Hanafi fiqh work and identify key features used to evaluate manuscript reliability.

Core Idea
Manuscript copies are the backbone of Hanafi textual transmission; their careful description ensures the integrity of the matn.

Before modern printing, the Hanafi fiqh tradition was transmitted through handwritten manuscripts. Scholars like the editor of Al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah meticulously list and describe these copies to establish a reliable critical edition. This lesson examines the criteria used to assess manuscript quality and why this matters for studying Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the purpose of the manuscript list
Understand that this list is part of the critical apparatus: it documents the sources used to reconstruct the text of Al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah. Each entry provides evidence for the editor's choices.
2
Identify key descriptive elements
Note details like date, folios, lines per page, script quality, and presence of vocalization (dabt). These help assess a manuscript's age, care, and accuracy.
For example, a manuscript with full vocalization (dabt) is considered more reliable for reading.
3
Distinguish complete vs. partial copies
Some manuscripts contain the entire work, others only a volume or part. Partial copies can still be valuable for cross-checking portions where complete copies are missing.
Manuscripts 10 and 11 are only the first part; manuscript 12 is only the second volume.
4
Evaluate the provenance and location
Knowing where the manuscript is housed (e.g., Feyzullah Efendi Library in Istanbul, King Saud University in Riyadh) allows scholars to access it for verification and indicates its chain of custody.
The mention of multiple copies in different libraries adds strength to the textual tradition.
5
Connect to the broader Hanafi textual tradition
This list is part of the science of tahqiq (critical editing) in Hanafi fiqh, which ensures that later commentaries and rulings are based on the correct matn. It demonstrates the scholarly rigor applied to safeguarding the school's transmitted knowledge.
Without such manuscript verification, errors could propagate and affect legal rulings derived from the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النُّسَخُ الخَطَّية المعتمدة
٣- نسخة بتاريخ ٩٧٧هـ، وتقع في ٤٠٠ ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ٢٣ سطراً، وفي كل سطر ١١ كلمة، ممتازة، وخطها جميل واضح، وليس فيها ضبط إلا نادراً، مصورة من مكتبة شيخ الإسلام فيض الله أفندي، في اسطنبول، ومنها صورة في مكتبة الملك عبد الله بن عبد العزيز التابعة لجامعة أم القرى. ٤- نسخة بتاريخ ٩٧٧هـ أيضاً، وتقع في ٣٦٤ ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ٣٣ سطراً، وفي كل سطر ١٢ كلمة، وهي نسخة ممتازة إلى حد ما، وخطها جميل واضح، وليس فيها ضبط، منها صورة في مركز جمعة الماجد بدبي، وأصلها في مكتبة الغازي خسرو بتركيا.
ويظهر أن مالكها كان له اشتغال واضح بها، ومراجعات كثيرة فيها، وقد وضع عليها بعض الحواشي والتعليقات المفيدة، وعليها تصحيحات لنصها، وفي جوانبها عناوين تُبرز مضمون الكتاب.
٥ - نسخة بتاريخ ١٠٣١هـ ، وتقع في ٣٤٥ ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ٣٣ سطراً، وفيها ضبط ممتاز لكثير من الكلمات، ووضع على متن القدوري خط يُميزه عن الجوهرة، تحریر وتثبت مع من نص مختصر القدوري، ومن هذه النسخة صورة مودعة في جامعة أم القرى بمكة المكرمة.
٦ ـ نسخة بتاريخ ١٠٤١هـ، وتقع في ٣١٤ ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ٣١ سطراً، وفي كل سطر ١٦ كلمة، وهي نسخة ممتازة إلى حد ما، وخطها جميل واضح، وفيها ضبط لكلماتها من أولها إلى ورقة ٥٥ فقط، مصورة من مكتبة شيخ الإسلام فيض الله أفندي في اسطنبول، ومنها صورة في مكتبة الملك عبد الله بن عبد العزيز، التابعة لجامعة أم القرى.
- نسخة بتاريخ ١٠٥٨هـ، وهي في جزءين، الأول برقم ١٢٤، ويقع في ٣٨٣ ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ٢٤ سطراً، والثاني برقم ١٢٥، ويقع في ٣٨٧ ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ٢٤ سطراً، ويبدأ بكتاب الوديعة، وهي نسخة تامة ممتازة، محفوظ أصلها في مكتبة الساقزلي، في مكتبة الملك عبد العزيز بالمدينة المنورة.
- نسخة بتاريخ ١٠٧٠هـ، وتقع في ٣٨١ ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ٣٣ سطراً، وصورتها مودعة في مركز الملك فيصل الخيري في الرياض.
٩- نسخة بتاريخ ١٠٩٧هـ، وتقع في ٣٩٢ ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ٣٣ سطراً، وهي نسخة جيدة، وأصلها محفوظ في مكتبة الشفا، في مكتبة الملك عبد العزيز بالمدينة المنورة، برقم ٤٤٧.
١٠ ـ نسخة منها الجزء الأول من الجوهرة فقط، بدون تاريخ للنسخ، وتقع في ١٨٥ ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ٢٩ سطراً، وصورتها مودعة في مركز جمعة الماجد في دبي، ليس فيها تاريخ للنسخ، وتحوي النصف الأول من الكتاب فقط إلى آخر كتاب المزارعة، وهي مليئة في أطرافها بحواش كثيرة مفيدة في إيضاح النص وشرحه، وخطها لا بأس به، وهي ملونة جميلة.
١١ـ نسخة منها الجزء الأول من الجوهرة فقط، بدون تاريخ للنسخ، وتقع في ٢٦٥ ورقة، وخطها جيد واضح، وصورتها مودعة في جامعة الملك سعود في الرياض، وقد انتهى هذا الجزء عند آخر كتاب الوكالة، أي ما يعادل ثلث الجوهرة.
١٢- نسخة بتاريخ ١٠٦٨هـ تقريباً، منها المجلد الثاني من الجوهرة فقط، وتقع في ٢٨٧ ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ٢٣ سطراً، وتبدأ بكتاب النكاح إلى آخر الجوهرة، وصورتها مودعة في مركز جمعة الماجد بدبي.
The Approved Manuscript Copies
3- Copy dated 977 AH, comprising 400 folios, each page 23 lines, each line 11 words, excellent, with beautiful clear script, rarely vocalized, photographed from the library of Sheikh al-Islam Feyzullah Efendi in Istanbul, and a copy in the King Abdullah bin Abdulaziz Library of Umm al-Qura University. 4- Copy also dated 977 AH, comprising 364 folios, each page 33 lines, each line 12 words, a fairly excellent copy, with beautiful clear script, not vocalized, a copy in Juma al-Majid Center in Dubai, original in the Ghazi Khusraw Library in Turkey. It appears that its owner had clear engagement with it, many revisions, some useful marginal notes and comments, corrections to its text, and side headings highlighting the book's content. 5- Copy dated 1031 AH, comprising 345 folios, each page 33 lines, with excellent vocalization of many words, and the text of al-Quduri was marked with a line distinguishing it from al-Jawhara, verified and confirmed against the text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and a copy is deposited at Umm al-Qura University in Mecca. 6- Copy dated 1041 AH, comprising 314 folios, each page 31 lines, each line 16 words, a fairly excellent copy, with beautiful clear script, vocalization from beginning to folio 55 only, photographed from the library of Sheikh al-Islam Feyzullah Efendi in Istanbul, and a copy in the King Abdullah bin Abdulaziz Library of Umm al-Qura University. - Copy dated 1058 AH, in two volumes, first numbered 124, comprising 383 folios, each page 24 lines, and second numbered 125, comprising 387 folios, each page 24 lines, beginning with the book of al-Wadi'ah, a complete excellent copy, original preserved in the Saqizli Library, in the King Abdulaziz Library in Medina. - Copy dated 1070 AH, comprising 381 folios, each page 33 lines, its copy deposited in the King Faisal Charitable Center in Riyadh. 9- Copy dated 1097 AH, comprising 392 folios, each page 33 lines, a good copy, original preserved in al-Shifa Library, in the King Abdulaziz Library in Medina, number 447. 10- Copy of only the first part of al-Jawhara, undated, comprising 185 folios, each page 29 lines, its copy deposited in Juma al-Majid Center in Dubai, no date of copying, contains only the first half of the book up to the end of the book of al-Muzara'ah, filled with many useful marginal notes clarifying the text and its explanation, its script is acceptable, colored and beautiful. 11- Copy of only the first part of al-Jawhara, undated, comprising 265 folios, its script good and clear, its copy deposited in King Saud University in Riyadh, this part ends at the end of the book of al-Wakalah, i.e., about one third of al-Jawhara. 12- Copy dated approximately 1068 AH, of only the second volume of al-Jawhara, comprising 287 folios, each page 23 lines, beginning with the book of al-Nikah to the end of al-Jawhara, its copy deposited in Juma al-Majid Center in Dubai.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographical list of the approved manuscript copies (al-nusakh al-khatiyyah al-mu'tamadah) of the book Al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The compiler enumerates twelve manuscripts, providing for each: the date of copying (mostly in the 10th-11th centuries AH), number of folios, lines per page, words per line, quality description, script characteristics, presence of vocalization (dabt), distinguishing features (such as marking the text of al-Quduri), location of the original and copies (e.g., libraries in Istanbul, Dubai, Riyadh, Medina, Mecca, etc.). The list begins with manuscript no. 3, indicating that the earlier numbers (1 and 2) were presumably listed on previous pages. The manuscripts vary in completeness: some contain the entire work, others only the first or second volume. This detailed description helps establish the textual basis for the critical edition.

Key Terms
نسخة خطية (nuskhah khatiyyah): A handwritten manuscript copy of the book.
ضبط (dabt): Vocalization of the Arabic text with diacritical marks.
متن القدوري (matn al-Quduri): The base text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text.
تحقيق (tahqiq): Critical edition of a classical text, involving collation of manuscripts.
حاشية (hashiyah): Marginal notes or glosses written by readers or scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Understanding the Manuscript: Al-Jawharat al-Nayyira and Its Transmission
Heading of manuscript copy used

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the manuscript copy of al-Jawharat al-Nayyira used in this edition and explain the significance of its date and the phrase 'relied-upon manuscript copies.'

Core Idea
The 1097 AH manuscript of al-Jawharat al-Nayyira is a primary source for authentic Hanafi fiqh transmission.

This lesson introduces the manuscript copy of al-Jawharat al-Nayyira, a key commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The date 1097 AH and the phrase 'relied-upon manuscript copies' anchor the authority of the text we will study. Understanding these details helps you appreciate the chain of transmission and editorial choices.

Guided Path
1
Read the heading
The heading states 'الجوهرة النيرة نسخة ١٠٩٧ هـ' and 'النُّسَخُ الخَطَّية المعتمدة'. Identify the title and the date.
The date is in the Islamic calendar (AH).
2
Interpret the date
1097 AH corresponds to approximately 1686 CE. Note that this is an Ottoman-period manuscript, indicating the era of copying.
3
Understand 'relied-upon copies'
This phrase indicates that the editor selected certain manuscripts as authoritative. Why is this important? It tells us that this copy is considered reliable for the textual tradition.
4
Connect to the commentary
Al-Jawharat al-Nayyira is by Imam al-Haddad. Recall that it is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi text.

The Critical Edition: Manuscript Sources and Method
Describes manuscript base and eclectic editorial method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the editor's method for reconstructing a sound text from multiple faulty manuscripts and evaluate its reliability.

Core Idea
No single manuscript is perfect; a sound text emerges from combining all witnesses critically.

This lesson introduces the editorial methodology behind the printed edition of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah. Understanding how the text was reconstructed helps us appreciate its authority and know its limitations. The editor's frank discussion of manuscript variation also teaches us important lessons about the transmission of Hanafi fiqh texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's manuscript base
Note that the editor used fourteen manuscript copies of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah. None alone was sufficient; each had errors, omissions, or distortions.
This is a common situation in editing classical texts—no single copy is perfect.
2
Analyze the editorial method
The editor combined all copies and cross-referenced with his earlier critical edition of Mukhtasar al-Quduri (the base text). He selected the best reading from among the witnesses to produce an eclectic text.
This is called the 'selected text' (al-nass al-mukhtar) method.
3
Consider the significance for textual authority
Because the edition is a reconstruction, it is not identical to any single original manuscript. However, the editor's transparency and critical use of multiple sources gives it high authority for study.
Always check the editor's introduction to assess the reliability of any critical edition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النسخ الخَطية المعتمدة، الجوهرة النيرة الجزء الثاني نسخة ١٠٦٨هـ تقريباً بتاريخ حسابي غريب.
منهج التحقيق:
١- لقد يسر الله تعالى لي من نسخ الجوهرة النيرة عدداً مباركاً، وصل إلى أربع عشرة نسخة، وهي متفاوتة في جودتها حساً ومعنى، وكمالاً ونقصاً، ومع هذا العدد لم أجد بينها نسخةً يصلح اتخاذها ركناً شديداً آوي إليه، فلكل نسخة علة ومشكلة، من أخطاء في النسخ، وتحريف للنص، ونقص بل أسقاط فيه، وتقديم وتأخير، وغير ذلك. هذا، لكنها بمجموعها كلها مضموماً إليها النص المحقق من مختصر القدوري الذي أكرمني الله بخدمته من قبل، ومع بذل الجهد والطاقة، وتوفيق الله تعالى أولاً وآخراً تم الوصول والله الحمد إلى نص سليم من الجوهرة بقدر الإمكان، وذلك على طريقة النص المختار من تلك النسخ كلها.
٢- لقد دعاني العمل على الجوهرة إلى مراجعة النسخ الخطية لمختصر القدوري المتن الذي شرح فيها، وقد لاحظت اختلاف نُسخ القدوري التي يسر الله لي جَمْعَها مع النسخة التي اعتمدها الحداد في شرحه هذا، وكذلك اختلاف نُسخ الجوهرة، وهكذا الحال فيما يسر الله لي من قبل من خدمة التراث في كتب عدة، كل هذا جعل قلبي مطمئناً تماماً لقضية اختلاف النسخ في الكتب، وأنه أمر طبيعي جداً، وواقعي حتى عند أئمتنا السابقين واللاحقين في نُسخ ما يكتبون ونُسخ ما ينقلون عنه.
The relied-upon manuscript copies. Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, part two, copy approximately 1068 AH by a strange chronological calculation. Methodology of editing: 1- Allah the Exalted has facilitated for me a blessed number of copies of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, amounting to fourteen copies. They vary in quality, form and meaning, perfection and deficiency. Despite this number, I did not find among them a single copy that could serve as a solid pillar to rely upon; each copy has a defect and a problem: errors in copying, distortion of text, deficiency, even omissions, forward and backward (displacement), and other issues. However, taken together, along with the edited text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri – which Allah honored me to serve previously – and with exertion of effort and energy, and with the success of Allah first and last, I have arrived, praise be to Allah, at a sound text of Al-Jawharah as much as possible, by the method of selecting the text from all those copies. 2- The work on Al-Jawharah led me to review the manuscript copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, the matn that is commented upon in it. I noticed the difference between the Quduri copies that Allah facilitated for me to collect and the copy that al-Haddad relied upon in this commentary, as well as the difference among the Jawharah copies. Likewise, it is the case with what Allah previously facilitated for me in serving heritage in several books. All of this made my heart fully at ease regarding the issue of textual variation in books, that it is a very natural and realistic matter, even among our early and later imams in the copies they wrote and the copies they transmitted from.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage from the editor's introduction explains the manuscript basis for the critical edition of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah. The editor states that he had access to fourteen manuscript copies, but none alone was sufficient due to errors, distortions, omissions, and transpositions. By combining all copies and cross-referencing with the previously edited Mukhtasar al-Quduri (the base text being commented upon), he reconstructed a sound text. He also notes that variation among manuscripts is natural and expected, even in the works of early scholars. This explanation is important for understanding the authority of the printed text: it is a reconstructed eclectic text, not a diplomatic copy of a single manuscript.

Key Terms
النص المختار (al-nass al-mukhtar): The selected text — the editor's choice among variant readings from multiple manuscripts.
نسخ خطية (nusukh khattiyyah): Handwritten manuscript copies of the book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Four
C) Fourteen
D) Forty

Key Takeaway
A critical edition is a scholarly reconstruction; always examine the editor's method and manuscript base before relying on a printed text.

Introduction and Front Matter

Critical Edition Methodology for Hanafi Texts
Editor's methodological introduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven steps the editor used to produce a reliable text of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira and explain why no single manuscript was sufficient.

Core Idea
No single manuscript is perfect; a reliable text emerges from collating all variants.

A critical edition of a classical Hanafi text like al-Jawhara al-Nayyira requires careful comparison of multiple handwritten copies. The editor explains why he needed fourteen manuscripts and how he combined them to produce a sound text. This lesson walks through his method so you can appreciate the scholarly work behind reliable printed editions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scale of the manuscript problem
The editor collected fourteen manuscripts, none complete or error-free. Each had scribal errors, distortions, omissions, or other defects. Recognize that such variation is natural and expected in handwritten transmission.
This is common for all classical Islamic texts.
2
Identify the 'selected text' method
Instead of relying on one 'best' manuscript, the editor used al-nass al-mukhtar: at each point he chose the reading that seemed strongest across all copies, aided by a previously edited version of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
This method balances multiple sources rather than elevating one.
3
List the seven editorial procedures
The editor lists seven specific steps: (1) placing the Mukhtasar text at the top of each page, (2) harmonizing the two texts, (3) marking the Mukhtasar in red, (4) noting only important variants, (5) formatting into paragraphs, (6) using asterisks for quotations, and (7) separating text from commentary.
Each step aims at clarity and usability for the reader.
4
Appreciate the role of previous scholarly work
The editor had previously edited Mukhtasar al-Quduri and its commentary al-Lubab. That earlier critical work provided a basis for the current edition.
Building on prior scholarship is essential in academic editing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منهج التحقيق
١- لقد يسر الله تعالى لي من نسخ الجوهرة النيرة عدداً مباركاً، وصل إلى أربع عشرة نسخة، وهي متفاوتة في جودتها حساً ومعناً، وكمالاً ومع هذا العدد لم أجد بينها نسخةً يصلح اتخاذها ركناً شديداً آوي إليه، فلكل نسخة علة ومشكلة، من أخطاء في النسخ، وتحريف للنص، ونقص بل إسقاط فيه، وتقديم وتأخير، وغير ذلك.
هذا، لكنها بمجموعها كلها مضموماً إليها النص المحقق من مختصر القدوري الذي أكرمني الله بخدمته من قبل، ومع بذل الجهد والطاقة، وتوفيق الله تعالى أولاً وآخراً تم الوصول والحمد لله إلى نص سليم من الجوهرة بقدر الإمكان، وذلك على طريقة النص المختار من تلك النسخ كلها.
٢- لقد دعاني العمل على الجوهرة إلى مراجعة النسخ الخطية لمختصر القدوري المتن الذي شرح فيها، وقد لاحظت اختلاف نسخ القدوري التي يسر الله لي جمعها مع النسخة التي اعتمدها الحداد في شرحه هذا، وكذلك اختلاف نسخ الجوهرة، وهكذا الحال فيما يسر الله لي من قبل من خدمة التراث في كتب عدة، كل هذا جعل قلبي مطمئناً تماماً لقضية اختلاف النسخ في الكتب، وأنه أمر طبيعي جداً، وواقعي حتى عند أئمتنا السابقين واللاحقين في نسخ ما يكتبون ونسخ ما ينقلون عنه.
٣- أثبت أعلى صفحات الجوهرة النيرة نص مختصر القدوري، مفصولاً بينهما بخط، معتمداً على النسخة المصححة التي توصلت إليها أيام اشتغالي بتحقيقه مع اللباب، والتي لا أزال أجتهد في تصحيحها، وسيجد القارئ اختلافاً يسيراً بين النسخة التي أثبتها أعلى، وبين النسخة المضمنة في الجوهرة التي اعتمدها الإمام الحداد؛ والسبب واضح.
٤- نسقت بين نسختي من مختصر القدوري مع الجوهرة، زيادة ونقصاً وصياغة وترتيباً؛ حيث إن نسخ الجوهرة لم يُميز فيها بين الشرح والمتن ويختلف المتن من نسخة إلى أخرى، وكان التداخل بينهما في النسخ هو الأصل إلا في مواضع يسيرة، ونبهت على الفوارق المهمة منها.
٥- قمت بتمييز نص مختصر القدوري المضمن في الجوهرة باللون الأحمر؛ لزيادة إبرازه، وسهولة الوقوف عليه.
٦- لم أشر إلى الفوارق بين نسخ الجوهرة إلا إلى المهم منها، مما له أثر في المعنى، وكذلك لم أشر إلى الإسقاط والتحريفات الواقعة في النسخ.
٧- قمت بتفقير النص، وجعله في جمل متفرقة، وكذلك جعلت بداية كل مسألة وفرع من أول السطر؛ إيضاحاً للنص، وتيسيراً للوقوف على مضمونه.
وضعت علامة نجمة في أول كل مقولة من مقولات القدوري التي يريد المؤلف شرحها، حين يقول: «قوله».
Methodology of the Critical Edition
1- Allah the Exalted has facilitated for me a blessed number of copies of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, amounting to fourteen copies, varying in quality in terms of material and meaning, and completeness. Despite this number, I did not find among them a single copy that could serve as a solid pillar to which I could resort, for every copy has a defect and a problem, such as errors in copying, distortion of the text, omission—even complete dropping—and inversion and delay, etc.
Nevertheless, taken as a whole, along with the critically edited text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri which Allah had previously honored me to serve, and with exertion of effort and energy, and with the success of Allah first and last, I have reached, praise be to Allah, a sound text of al-Jawhara as much as possible, using the method of choosing the text from among all those copies.
2- Working on al-Jawhara led me to review the manuscripts of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, the text which is explained in it, and I noticed the differences between the copies of al-Quduri that Allah facilitated for me to collect and the copy that al-Haddad used in his commentary, as well as differences among copies of al-Jawhara. Likewise, in what Allah facilitated for me before in serving heritage in several books, all this made me completely confident about the issue of variant readings in books, and that it is a very natural and realistic matter, even among our earlier and later imams in the copies they wrote and the copies of those from whom they transmitted.
3- I placed above the pages of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira the text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, separated by a line, relying on the corrected copy that I arrived at during my work on its critical edition with al-Lubab, which I am still striving to correct. The reader will find a slight difference between the copy I placed above and the copy embedded in al-Jawhara that Imam al-Haddad relied on; the reason is clear.
4- I harmonized my copy of Mukhtasar al-Quduri with that of al-Jawhara, in terms of additions, omissions, phrasing, and arrangement, because the copies of al-Jawhara did not distinguish between the commentary and the text, and the text differs from one copy to another. Intermixing between them was the norm except in a few places, and I pointed out the important discrepancies among them.
5- I marked the text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri embedded in al-Jawhara in red to enhance its visibility and make it easy to identify.
6- I did not indicate the discrepancies among copies of al-Jawhara except for the important ones that affect meaning, and likewise I did not indicate the omissions and distortions occurring in the copies.
7- I sectioned the text into separate sentences, and also made the beginning of each issue and branch start from the beginning of the line for clarity and ease of understanding the content.
I placed an asterisk at the beginning of each statement of al-Quduri that the author intends to explain when he says: “His statement.”
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction describing his methodology for establishing the critical text of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. He begins by stating that he collected fourteen manuscripts of al-Jawhara, none of which was perfect alone, but by collating them and using the previously edited Mukhtasar al-Quduri, he produced a sound text via the method of 'selected text' (al-nass al-mukhtar). He emphasizes that manuscript variation is natural and expected. He then lists seven specific editorial procedures: (1) placing the Mukhtasar al-Quduri text at the top of each page separated by a line, (2) harmonizing his Mukhtasar text with the embedded text in al-Jawhara, (3) marking the Mukhtasar text in red for clarity, (4) noting only important textual differences, (5) formatting the text into separate sentences and paragraphs, and (6) placing an asterisk before each quote from al-Quduri. This methodology reflects standard Hanafi manuscript editing practice.

Key Terms
الجوهرة النيرة (al-Jawhara al-Nayyira): The title of the commentary by al-Haddad on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, which is the subject of this critical edition.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The famous Hanafi fiqh manual by Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri, which al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explains.
النص المختار (al-nass al-mukhtar): The method of selecting the best reading from among multiple manuscript variants to establish a reliable text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What method did the editor use to establish the final text of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira?
A) He relied on a single manuscript.
B) He selected the best readings from multiple manuscripts.
C) He invented the text himself.
D) He used only one printed edition.

Key Takeaway
A reliable critical edition of a Hanafi text requires collating multiple manuscripts and choosing the best reading at each point.

Understanding the Editor's Methodology in Al-Jawharah Al-Nayyirah
Editor explains his critical methodology for establishing the text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate a critical edition of a Hanafi fiqh text by analyzing the editor's methodological choices presented in this front matter.

Core Idea
Critical editions of Hanafi texts require methodical selection and correction of manuscripts, not mere reproduction.

This lesson explores the front matter of the critical edition of Al-Jawharah Al-Nayyirah, where the editor details his methodology. Understanding these choices is essential for assessing the reliability of the edition in your studies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's primary textual method
The editor states he used the 'selected text' method (al-nass al-mukhtar). Understand what this means: choosing a base manuscript and correcting it against others, rather than following one manuscript blindly or creating an eclectic reconstruction.
This is a common approach in scholarly editions of classical texts.
2
Analyze the visual layout decisions
The editor placed the matn (Mukhtasar al-Quduri) at the top of each page, separated from the sharh (commentary) by a line, and highlighted it in red. Consider why these choices improve usability for a student of Hanafi fiqh.
Earlier editions did not distinguish between text and commentary.
3
Examine the editor's handling of textual variants
The editor only notes important differences that affect meaning, ignoring minor scribal errors and omissions. Evaluate the scholarly rationale for this selective approach.
Complete apparatus can distract; this edition prioritizes readability.
4
Assess the decision to omit comment on tarjihat and mufta bihi
The editor explicitly refrains from discussing the author's tarjihat (preferences) within the madhhab or identifying the mufta bihi. He considers this a separate, complex issue. Debate whether this omission helps or hinders the reader.
The editor has a separate research on this topic.
5
Review the supplementary scholarly apparatus
The editor includes takhrij of hadith and athar, attribution of quotes to sources, a biography of the author, and a comparative study with the source text Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Understand how each element supports a critical reading.
This apparatus is typical of high-quality critical editions.

منهج التحقيق
ومن هنا رأيتُ أن الاعتماد على طريقة النص المختار هي الطريقة الأسلم في إثبات نص صحيح للكتاب المحقق، والله أعلم. ٣- أثبتُ أعلى صفحات الجوهرة النيرة نص مختصر القدوري، مفصولاً بينهما بخط، معتمداً على النسخة المصححة التي توصلت إليها أيام اشتغالي بتحقيقه مع اللباب، والتي لا أزال أجتهد في تصحيحها، وسيجد القارئ اختلافاً يسيراً بين النسخة التي أثبتها أعلى، وبين النسخة المضمنة في الجوهرة التي اعتمدها الإمام الحداد ؛ والسبب واضح. النسخة المضمنة ٤- نسقت بين نسختي من مختصر القدوري مع الجوهرة، زيادة ونقصاً وصياغة وترتيباً؛ حيث إن نُسخ الجوهرة لم يُميّز فيها بين الشرح والمتن ويختلف المتن من نسخة إلى أخرى، وكان التداخل بينهما في النسخ هو الأصل إلا في مواضع يسيرة، ونبهت على الفوارق المهمة منها. ه قمت بتمييز نص مختصر القدوري المضمن في الجوهرة باللون الأحمر ؛ لزيادة إبرازه، وسهولة الوقوف عليه.
٦- لم أشر إلى الفوارق بين نُسخ الجوهرة إلا إلى المهم منها، مما له أثر في المعنى، وكذلك لم أشر إلى الأسقاط والتحريفات الواقعة في النُّسَخ. - قمت بتفقير النص، وجعله في جُمَلٍ متفرقة، وكذلك جعلتُ بداية كل مسألة وفرع من أول السطر ؛ إيضاحاً للنص، وتيسيراً للوقوف على مضمونه.
وضعت علامة نجمة في أول كل مقولة من مقولات القدوري التي يريد المؤلف شرحها، حين يقول: «قوله».
٨ - ضبطتُ ما أشكل من النص، ولم أكثر من ذلك ملاحظاً حال قارىء هذا الكتاب وأمثاله ممن بلغ رتبة كريمة في العلم. ١٠- وضعتُ للنص علامات الترقيم المشهورة؛ سعياً لإدراك النص وفهمه، ومعرفة المراد منه، في حين كان النص في طبعاته السابقة يسير سير السواني [؟] لا ينقطع.
١١- شرحتُ بلُطف الكلمات الغريبة التي قدرت حاجة قارئ هذا الكتاب وأمثاله إليها.
١٢- آثرتُ عدم التعليق على ما يذكره المؤلف من ترجيحات في المذهب، وبيان للمفتى به؛ لأن هذه القضية مسألة طويلة شائكة، ومختلف فيها بين علماء المذهب، وقد بيّنتُ الاختلاف فيها بالتفصيل في بحثي المسمى: «تكوين المذهب الحنفي، مع تأملات في ضوابط المفتى به»، وهو قيد الطبع، تمم الله بالخير.
١٣- قمتُ بتخريج مع الاجتهاد في نقل بيان درجته والحكم عليه من كلام أهل الأحاديث والآثار الواردة في النص على سبيل الاختصار، الشأن في ذلك.
١٤- قمتُ بعزو النصوص التي نقلها المصنف في الجوهرة إلى مصادرها، بذكر الجزء والصفحة إن كان المصدر مطبوعاً، دون المخطوط.
سبيلاً.
١٥ - ترجمت للمؤلف رحمه الله ترجمةً موسعة بما استطعت إلى ذلك
١٦- قمت بدراسة علمية عن الجوهرة وأصلها السراج الوهاج، وذكرت مقارنة بينهما، مع الإتيان بنماذج ونصوص من كل من الكتابين.
Methodology of Verification
From here I saw that relying on the method of the selected text (al-nass al-mukhtar) is the safest method for establishing a correct text of the verified book, and Allah knows best. 3- I placed at the top of the pages of Al-Jawharah Al-Nayyirah the text of Mukhtasar Al-Quduri, separated between them by a line, relying on the corrected copy that I arrived at during my work of verifying it with Al-Lubab, and which I still strive to correct. The reader will find a slight difference between the copy I placed at the top and the copy included in Al-Jawharah that Imam Al-Haddad relied upon; the reason is clear. The included copy 4- I reconciled between my two copies of Mukhtasar Al-Quduri and Al-Jawharah, in terms of addition, omission, formulation, and arrangement; since the copies of Al-Jawharah did not distinguish between the commentary and the text, and the text differs from one copy to another, and overlap between them in the copies was the norm except in a few places, and I alerted to the important differences among them. 5- I distinguished the text of Mukhtasar Al-Quduri included in Al-Jawharah in red color to further highlight it and make it easy to refer to.
6- I did not point out differences between copies of Al-Jawharah except the important ones that affect the meaning, and likewise I did not point to omissions and distortions occurring in the copies. - I divided the text into paragraphs and made it into separate sentences, and also made the beginning of each issue and subsection from the start of the line to clarify the text and facilitate understanding its content. I placed an asterisk at the beginning of every statement of Al-Quduri that the author wants to explain when he says: 'his statement'.
8- I vocalized what was obscure in the text, and did not do much of that, observing the situation of the reader of this book and his like who have reached a noble rank in knowledge. 10- I placed punctuation marks for the text, striving to grasp and understand the text and know its intended meaning, whereas the text in its previous editions flowed like a stream without interruption.
11- I gently explained unusual words that I deemed the reader of this book and his like need.
12- I preferred not to comment on what the author mentions of preferences (tarjihat) in the madhhab and the clarification of the mufta bihi (operative ruling); because this issue is a long and thorny matter, and there is disagreement about it among the scholars of the madhhab. I have detailed the disagreement in my research entitled: 'Formation of the Hanafi Madhhab, with Reflections on the Controls of the Mufta Bihi', which is in the process of publication, may Allah complete it with goodness.
13- I undertook the takhrij (reference grading) with effort in reporting its grade and ruling based on the statements of the people of hadith and traditions (athar) mentioned in the text briefly, as is customary in that regard.
14- I attributed the texts that the author transmitted in Al-Jawharah to their sources, mentioning the part and page if the source is printed, but not for manuscripts.
A way.
15- I provided a extensive biography of the author, may Allah have mercy on him, to the extent I was able.
16- I conducted a scientific study of Al-Jawharah and its original Al-Siraj Al-Wahhaj, and mentioned a comparison between them, along with bringing models and texts from each of the two books.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is the front matter of the critical edition, specifically the editor's methodology (منهج التحقيق). The editor explains his approach to establishing a reliable text of Al-Jawharah Al-Nayyirah, a Hanafi fiqh commentary on Mukhtasar Al-Quduri. He adopts the 'selected text' method (النص المختار), which involves choosing a preferred base manuscript and correcting it against others. He places the matn (text of Mukhtasar Al-Quduri) at the top of each page, separated from the commentary below. He reconciles two copes—one he established and the one in the original Al-Jawharah used by Imam al-Haddad. He uses red color to highlight the matn, divides the text into paragraphs, and adds punctuation for clarity. He vocalizes obscure words and explains rare terms. Notably, he refrains from commenting on the author's tarjihat (preferences) within the Hanafi madhhab and the identification of the mufta bihi (operative ruling), considering it a complex topic requiring separate treatment. He also provides takhrij (source grading) for hadiths and athar, attributes citations to their sources, includes a biography of the author (likely Imam al-Haddad), and adds a comparative study of Al-Jawharah and its original work Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. This methodology ensures that the edition is scholarly and useful for advanced students of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
النص المختار (al-nass al-mukhtar): The editor's chosen method of relying on a selected base manuscript rather than following a single manuscript or eclectic approach.
المفتى به (al-mufta bihi): The relied-upon ruling in the Hanafi madhhab, used for issuing fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the editor's primary method for establishing the correct text of Al-Jawharah Al-Nayyirah?
A) Following a single manuscript exactly as found.
B) Using an eclectic approach without a base manuscript.
C) Relying on a selected text (النص المختار) with corrections.
D) Reconstructing the text from later commentaries.

Key Takeaway
A critical edition's methodology—especially the choice of base manuscript, treatment of variants, and supplementary apparatus—determines its reliability as a tool for studying Hanafi fiqh.

Introduction and Front Matter

Editor's Methodology for a Critical Edition of a Hanafi Fiqh Text
Editor's methodology for critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key editorial decisions in a critical edition of a Hanafi fiqh text and explain the rationale behind the editor's restraint regarding tarjīḥāt.

Core Idea
A critical edition restores the text; the editor refrains from inserting his own juristic preferences.

This lesson examines the methodology of a modern critical edition of a classical Hanafi fiqh text, al-Jawharah al-Nīrah. The editor, Dr. Sāʼid Bakdāsh, outlines eighteen points that reveal his scholarly approach. Understanding these decisions is crucial for appreciating how such editions serve both textual fidelity and the broader Hanafi tradition, especially regarding the delicate issue of preferred positions (tarjīḥāt) within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's primary textual interventions
From points 9–11, list what the editor did to the text itself: correcting ambiguities, adding punctuation, and explaining difficult words.
Note that he corrected only what was 'problematic' and did not over-edit.
2
Analyze the editor's restraint on tarjīḥāt
Examine point 12: why did the editor choose not to comment on the author's preferred positions? Identify the reason given and the separate work where he addresses this.
This restraint is a deliberate scholarly choice, not a shortcoming.
3
Examine the editor's methodology for hadith and source verification
Points 13–14: what is takhrīj? How does the editor trace sources? Distinguish between printed and manuscript sources.
He provides brief grading of hadith from the words of the experts.
4
Assess the editor's comprehensive study of the text
Points 15–18: the editor includes a biography, a comparison with the original work (al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj), a defense of the text's status, and introductions to sources and less-known figures. Why are these important?
These elements place the edition within the scholarly tradition while keeping the main text uncluttered.
5
Reflect on the overall purpose of the critical edition
Synthesize: how do these editorial choices serve the reader and the Hanafi madhhab? The editor aims to produce a reliable text that allows the reader to focus on fiqh without being distracted or misled.
The edition is a tool for studying fiqh directly, not a work of juristic commentary.

Methodology of Investigation
9- I corrected what was problematic in the text, and did not exceed that, observing the condition of the reader of this book and his like who have attained a noble rank in knowledge. 10- I placed well-known punctuation marks for the text; striving to comprehend the text, understand it, and know its intended meaning, whereas the text in its previous editions ran like a continuous stream without interruption.
11- I gently explained the unfamiliar words that I estimated the reader of this book and his like would need.
12- I preferred not to comment on what the author mentions of preferred positions (tarjīḥāt) in the madhhab and clarification of what is given for fatwa, because this issue is a long and thorny matter, and there is disagreement among the scholars of the madhhab. I have detailed the disagreement in my research entitled: 'Takwīn al-Madhhab al-Ḥanafī, with Reflections on the Controls of the Muftā bihi', which is in print, may Allah complete it with good.
13- I undertook takhrīj (source verification) with effort in transmitting the statement of its grade and ruling from the words of the people of ḥadīth and āthār (traditions) that appear in the text briefly, as is the custom in that regard.
14- I attributed the texts that the author transmitted in al-Jawharah to their sources, mentioning the volume and page if the source is printed, not the manuscript.
15- I prepared an extensive biography of the author, may Allah have mercy on him, as far as I was able.
16- I conducted a scientific study of al-Jawharah and its original al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj, and mentioned a comparison between them, bringing examples and texts from each of the two books.
Methodology of Investigation
79
17- I explained the author's methodology in al-Jawharah al-Nīrah, along with clarifying the status of the book al-Jawharah in the Ḥanafī madhhab, and the extent of its reliance and acceptance among the scholars of the madhhab, discussing and refuting the statement of those who considered it among the weak and non-reliable books.
18- I briefly introduced the sources that the author transmitted from, as well as the less famous figures mentioned in al-Jawharah, and I placed that in the study section; to lighten the footnotes from them, and to avoid distracting the reader from the fiqh of issues and branches.
*****
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is the editor's methodology (manhaj al-taḥqīq) for the critical edition. It lists eighteen points (points 9-18 are presented here) detailing the editorial choices. The editor, Dr. Sāʼid Bakdāsh, explains his approach: he corrected textual ambiguities without over-editing, added punctuation to aid comprehension, glossed difficult terms, and deliberately refrained from commenting on the author's tarjīḥāt (preferred positions) within the Ḥanafī madhhab, as he has separately studied the topic of 'al-muftā bihi' in his work 'Takwīn al-Madhhab al-Ḥanafī'. This restraint is typical of critical editors who wish to present the text as-is without superimposing later juristic preferences. He also performed takhrīj of ḥadīth and āthār, traced sources, provided an author biography, compared al-Jawharah with its source al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj, clarified al-Jawharah's status in the Ḥanafī school, and introduced lesser-known figures. All of this serves to place the edition within the scholarly tradition while leaving the fiqh rulings for the reader to study directly.

Key Terms
الجوهرة النيرة (al-Jawharah al-Nīrah): The title of the commentary being edited; a Hanafi fiqh text by Imam al-Ḥaddād.
السراج الوهاج (al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj): The original work upon which al-Jawharah al-Nīrah is a commentary.
المذهب الحنفي (al-madhhab al-ḥanafī): The Hanafi school of Islamic law; the context of the book.
المفتى به (al-muftā bihi): The relied-upon ruling for issuing fatwas; the operative position in the madhhab.
ترجيحات (tarjīḥāt): Preferred positions within the madhhab; choices among differing opinions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the editor, why did he choose not to comment on the author's tarjīḥāt in the madhhab?
A) Because he lacked knowledge of Hanafi juristic preferences.
B) Because the issue is complex and disputed among Hanafi scholars, and he has treated it separately.
C) Because the author's tarjīḥāt are already correct and need no comment.
D) Because he wanted to keep the edition short.

Key Takeaway
A critical edition of a Hanafi fiqh text balances textual restoration with scholarly restraint, allowing the original author's fiqh to speak without later interpretive interference.

Navigating the Sources: The Bibliography of Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira
Bibliography of sources for the critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of sources used in a Hanafi fiqh critical edition and explain the value of early Hanafi works and later commentaries.

Core Idea
A critical edition's bibliography is a roadmap to the Hanafi tradition—from the earliest works to later commentaries.

This lesson examines the bibliography at the beginning of the critical edition of Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. While it may seem like a mere list, it reveals the scholarly lineage of Hanafi fiqh. Understanding these sources helps you appreciate the depth and authenticity of the legal rulings you study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the earliest Hanafi sources
Look for works by Abu Hanifa's direct students like Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, such as the two "al-Athar" entries. These are primary sources for the Hanafi school.
These are from the 2nd century AH, foundational for understanding the school's origins.
2
Distinguish between primary and secondary sources
Note which works are original texts (like al-Mukhtar) and which are commentaries (like al-Ikhtiyar li-Ta'lil al-Mukhtar). This shows how later scholars built upon earlier works.
3
Recognize the diversity of disciplines
The bibliography includes hadith (e.g., al-Adab al-Mufrad), siyar (al-Ahkam al-Sultaniyya), ikhtilaf (al-Ishraf), and tafsir (Asbab al-Nuzul). This demonstrates the interdisciplinary nature of fiqh.
A well-rounded faqih draws from multiple Islamic sciences.
4
Apply the bibliography to your own research
Use this model to find reliable Hanafi references. For example, when researching a ruling, start with early matn, then consult a sharh, and finally check a critical edition's sources.
This skill is essential for independent study and verifying rulings.

فهرس مصادر التحقيق
١ - الآثار، لأبي يوسف يعقوب بن إبراهيم، ت۱۸۲ هـ، اعتنى به الشيخ أبو الوفا الأفغاني، تصوير دار الكتب العلمية، بيروت.
٢ ـ الآثار، محمد بن الحسن الشيباني، ت ١٨٩ هـ، إدارة القرآن الكريم وعلومه كراتشي، باكستان، ط ١٤٠٧/١هـ.
٣ ـ إتحاف السادة المتقين بشرح أسرار إحياء علوم الدين، للزبيدي محمد بن محمد ، ت ١٢٠٥هـ، دار الفكر.
٤ ـ أثر الحديث الشريف في اختلاف الأئمة الفقهاء رضي الله عنهم، محمد عوامة، دار اليسر المدينة المنورة، ط١٤٢٨/٥هـ.
هـ ـ الأحاديث المختارة للضياء المقدسي محمد بن عبد الواحد، ت ٦٤٣هـ تحقيق د/ عبد الملك بن دهيش مكتبة النهضة الحديثة، مكة المكرمة، ط١٤١٦/١هـ.
٦ ـ الأحكام السلطانية والولايات الدينية، للماوردي علي بن محمد، ت ٤٥٠ هـ، دار الكتب العلمية، بيروت، ١٣٩٨هـ.
ـ أخبار مكة في قديم الدهر وحديثه للفاكهي محمد بن إسحاق، ت ۲۷۲هـ تحقيق د/ عبد الملك بن دهيش مكتبة النهضة الحديثة، مكة المكرمة، ط١٤٠٧/١هـ.
- أخبار مكة وما جاء فيها من الآثار للأزرقي محمد بن عبد الله ، ت ٢٤٤هـ، تحقيق رشدي صالح ،ملحس دار الثقافة، مكة المكرمة، ط١٤٠٣/٤هـ.
۹ - الاختيار لتعليل المختار للموصلي عبد الله بن محمود، ت ٦٨٣هـ ، ط دار المعرفة، بيروت، صورة عن طبعة محمود أبو دقيقة.
١٠ - الأدب المفرد للبخاري محمد بن إسماعيل، ت٢٥٦هـ، تحقيق خالد بن عبد الرحمن العك، دار المعرفة، بيروت، ط ١٤٢٠/٢هـ.
١١ ـ الأذكار من كلام سيد الأبرار صلى الله عليه وسلم، للنووي الدين يحيى بن شرف، ت ٦٧٦هـ، دار المنهاج، بيروت، ط١٤٢٥/١هـ.
١٢ ـ الأربعون النووية (مع شرحه جامع العلوم والحكم، لابن رجب الحنبلي)، للنووي محيي الدين يحيى بن شرف ت ٦٧٦هـ، تحقيق شعيب الأرناؤط، وإبراهيم باجس، ط١٤٢٣/٩هـ (طبعـة خاصـة بـدارة الملك عبد العزيز بالرياض).
١٣ ـ أسباب النزول للواحدي علي بن أحمد، ت٤٦٨هـ، تحقيق د / مصطفى البغا دار ابن كثير دمشق، ط١٤٠٨/١هـ.
١٤ ـ أسنى المطالب شرح روض الطالب، زكريا بـن محمــد الأنصاري، ت٩٢٦هـ، المكتبة الإسلامية.
١٥ ـ الإشراف على نكت مسائل الخلاف القاضي عبد الوهاب بـن علي المالكي، ت٤٢٢هـ، تحقيق الحبيب بن طاهر، دار ابن حزم، بيروت، ط١٤٢٠/١هـ.
١٦ ـ الإصابة في تمييز الصحابة لابن حجر العسقلاني أحمد بـن بن

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a bibliography (فهرس مصادر التحقيق) listing the sources used by the critical editor of 'الجوهرة النيرة'. It includes classical Hanafi works (e.g., 'الآثار' by Abu Yusuf and al-Shaybani), hadith collections, and later commentaries. This front matter provides the scholarly foundation for the edition. Students should note the diversity of sources, including early Hanafi texts and later reference works.

Key Terms
الآثار (al-Athar): A collection of hadith and legal opinions attributed to early Hanafi imams, often transmitted by Abu Yusuf or Muhammad al-Shaybani.
فهرس مصادر التحقيق (fihris masadir al-tahqiq): Bibliography of sources used in a critical edition, listing manuscripts and printed editions.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
7 min
Navigating a Hanafi Bibliography: Understanding the Sources of al-Jawharat al-Nayyira
Listing the sources referenced in the editor's critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key Hanafi source works from a critical edition bibliography and classify them by their authority level (Zahir al-Riwayah, later commentary, etc.).

Core Idea
A critical edition's bibliography is a treasure map to the authoritative layers of the Hanafi school.

This lesson introduces you to the bibliography from the critical edition of al-Jawharat al-Nayyira. While this is not a legal ruling, it is an essential scholarly tool. Understanding how to read such a bibliography allows you to trace the chain of authority (isnad) of Hanafi knowledge, from the earliest sources to modern scholarship. Just as a jurist relies on reliable texts, a researcher must know which texts are authoritative and how they relate to each other.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genre
Recognize that this passage is a bibliography (fihris masadir) listing works used by the editor. It is not a fiqh ruling. The numbered entries continue from earlier pages.
Bibliographies often include works from different genres: hadith, fiqh, usul, lughah, etc.
2
Name the works and authors
Scan the entries for familiar works by al-Shaybani (al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir), Abu Yusuf (al-Kharaj), and later commentators like al-Tahtawi. Note the editors and publication details.
Pay attention to the death dates (t) to situate the author chronologically.
3
Classify by authority level
Categorize each work as: Zahir al-Riwayah (e.g., al-Jami' al-Saghir), Nawadir, later fatwa works (e.g., Hashiyat al-Tahtawi), or non-Hanafi sources (e.g., al-Hawi by al-Mawardi).
This classification helps assess the weight of the source in Hanafi jurisprudence.
4
Evaluate the editor's methodology
Observe that the editor, Dr. Sa'id Bakdash, includes both classical texts and modern critical editions, showing a scholarly approach. The presence of works like al-Jawhar al-Naqi indicates direct engagement with earlier scholarship.
A critical edition's bibliography reveals the editor's source base and scholarly rigor.
