Commentary
This passage is a bibliography (فهرس مصادر التحقيق) from the critical edition of al-Jawharat al-Nayyira. It lists the sources the editor, Dr. Sa'id Bakdash, used in preparing the text. The entries are numbered from 49 to 68, continuing from earlier pages. They include major works of hadith (e.g., al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir by al-Shaybani), fiqh (e.g., al-Hawi by al-Mawardi), Qur'anic exegesis (al-Jami' li-Ahkam al-Qur'an), Hanafi biographical works (al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya), and later commentaries and glosses (hashiyas) like those of al-Tahtawi and Qalyubi. The presence of al-Shaybani's books confirms the reliance on the Zahir al-Riwayah. This section shows the scholarly apparatus typical of modern academic editions of classical Hanafi texts.

Key Terms
الجامع الصغير (al-Jami' al-Saghir): One of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, containing foundational Hanafi rulings.
الجواهر المضية في طبقات الحنفية (al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya fi Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya): A biographical dictionary of Hanafi jurists by al-Qurashi, used for identifying scholars and their ranks.
حاشية الطحطاوي (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi): A gloss by Ahmad al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah by al-Shurunbulali, a later Hanafi fiqh manual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The bibliography of a critical edition reveals the scholarly chain (isnad) of Hanafi knowledge, from Zahir al-Riwayah to modern scholarship.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating a Hanafi Critical Edition Bibliography
Bibliography of sources for critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of sources (matn, sharh, hashiya, hadith, tafsir) listed in a Hanafi critical edition bibliography and explain the significance of Radd al-Muhtar as the key reference for fatwa in the later Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A critical edition's bibliography reveals the scholarly chain: matn, sharh, hashiya, and the auxiliary sources that support tarjih.

This lesson examines the bibliography of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyarah. It lists 87 sources used to verify the text. Understanding this list helps you see how later Hanafi scholars built upon earlier texts. You will learn to distinguish between primary matns, commentaries, super-commentaries, and supporting hadith works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main text being edited
Determine the base text and its commentary. Here, the base is Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and the commentary is Al-Jawharah al-Nayyarah.
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational Hanafi matn written by Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH).
2
Categorize sources by type
Look for matns, commentaries (sharh), super-commentaries (hashiya), hadith collections, tafsir, and biographical works. For example, Al-Durr al-Mukhtar is a sharh; Radd al-Muhtar is a hashiya.
Radd al-Muhtar = Hashiyat Ibn 'Abidin, the authoritative super-commentary for later Hanafi fatwa.
3
Note author death dates
Arrange sources chronologically to understand the development of Hanafi scholarship. Early works (e.g., Khulasat al-Dala'il, d. 598 AH) to later works (e.g., Radd al-Muhtar, d. 1252 AH).
Later works often incorporate or critique earlier ones, reflecting the tarjih process.
4
Identify key Hanafi reference works
Recognize core Hanafi texts like Al-Hidayah, Al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and Radd al-Muhtar. These are cited for authoritative positions.
Al-Hidayah appears in entry 71 via its hadith takhrij work (Al-Diraya).
5
Assess geographic and scholarly range
Observe the diversity of publication places (Aleppo, Kazan, Beirut, India, etc.) indicating the global reach of Hanafi scholarship.
This demonstrates that the critical edition draws on both Eastern and Western scholarly traditions.

۷۱ - الدراية في تخريج أحاديث الهداية، لابن حجر العسقلاني أحمد ابن علي، ت٨٥٢هـ، تصحيح عبد الله هاشم اليماني، دار المعرفة، بيروت.
۷۲ ـ الدر المختار شرح تنوير الأبصار ، للحصكفي محمد بن علي، ت ۱۰۸۸ هـ = رد المحتار.
٧٣ ـ الدر المنثور في التفسير بالمأثور، للسيوطي جلال الدين عبد الرحمن، ت۹۱۱هـ، دار الفكر، بيروت، ط١٤٠٣/١ هـ.
٧٤ ـ دلائل النبوة، للبيهقي أحمد بن الحسين، ت٤٥٨هـ، تحقيق د/ عبد المعطي قلعجي، دار الكتب العلمية، بيروت، ١٤٠٥هـ.
٧٥ - رد المحتار (حاشية ابن عابدين محمد أمين عابدين، ت ١٢٥٢هـ، البابي الحلبي، ط١٣٨٦/٢ هـ + ط دمشق، تحقيق د/ حسام الدين بن محمد صالح فرفور وآخرين، دار الثقافة، دمشق، ١٤٢١/١هـ.
٧٦ ـ روح المعاني في تفسير القرآن والسبع المثاني، الآلوسي شهاب الدين محمود بن عبد الله ، ت١٢٧٠هـ ، دار إحياء التراث العربي، بيروت، صورة عن الطبعة الميمنية.
۷۷ ـ الروض المربع شرح زاد المستقنع للبهوتي منصور بن يونس، ت ١٠٥١هـ، دار الكتب العلمية، بيروت، ط١٤٠٨/٩هـ.
۷۸ ـ روضة الطالبين وعمدة المفتين، للنووي محيي الدين، ت ٦٧٦هـ، المكتب الإسلامي، بيروت، ط١٤١٢/٣هـ.
۷۹ - الزهد والرقائق، عبد الله بن المبارك، تحقيق حبيب الرحمن الأعظمي، ط الهند، ١٣٨٥هـ.
۸۰ - الزوائد على سنن ابن ماجه للبوصيري أحمد بن أبي بكر، ٨٤٠هـ ، = سنن ابن ماجه.
٨١ ـ الزواجر عن اقتراف الكبائر، لابن حجر الهيتمي أحمـد بـن محمد، ت٩٧٤هـ ، دار المعرفة، بيروت، ١٤٠٢هـ.
۸۲ - سبل الهدى والرشاد في سيرة خير العباد صلى الله عليه وسلم، للصالحي محمد بن يوسف، ت ٩٤٢هـ ، دار الكتب العلمية، ١٤١٤/١هـ.
٨٣ ـ السراج المنير شرح الجامع الصغير، (للسيوطي)، للعزيزي علي ابن أحمد، ت ١٠٧٠هـ، القاهرة.
٨٤ - السراج الوهاج الموضح لكل طالب محتاج (شرح مختصر القدوري)، للحدادي أبي بكر بن علي، ت ٨٠٠هـ، (مخطوط).
٨٥ ـ السعاية في كشف ما في شرح الوقاية، اللكنـوي محمد عبد الحي، ت ١٣٠٤ هـ ، لاهور، باكستان، ١٣٩٦هـ.
٨٦ ـ سنن ابن ماجه، محمد بن يزيد القزويني، ت ٢٧٥ هـ، تحقيق محمد فؤاد عبد الباقي.
۸۷ - سنن أبي داود، سليمان بن الأشعث السجستاني، ت ٢٧٥ هـ، تحقيق الشيخ محمد عوامة، دار المنهاج جدة، ط٣/ ١٤٣١هـ.
69. Khulasat Tadhhib Tahdhib al-Kamal by al-Khazraji Ahmad ibn 'Abd Allah, died after 923 AH, published by Maktab al-Matbu'at al-Islamiyyah, Aleppo, 1411 AH, under supervision of 'Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah.
70. Khulasat al-Dala'il fi Tanqih al-Masa'il (Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri), by al-Razi 'Ali ibn Ahmad Makki, died 598 AH, printed in Kazan, Russia, 1318 AH.
71. Al-Diraya fi Takhrij Ahadith al-Hidaya, by Ibn Hajar al-'Asqalani Ahmad ibn 'Ali, died 852 AH, corrected by 'Abd Allah Hashim al-Yamani, Dar al-Ma'rifa, Beirut.
72. Al-Durr al-Mukhtar Sharh Tanwir al-Absar, by al-Haskafi Muhammad ibn 'Ali, died 1088 AH = Radd al-Muhtar.
73. Al-Durr al-Manthur fi al-Tafsir bi al-Ma'thur, by al-Suyuti Jalal al-Din 'Abd al-Rahman, died 911 AH, Dar al-Fikr, Beirut, 1st edition 1403/1 AH.
74. Dala'il al-Nubuwwa, by al-Bayhaqi Ahmad ibn al-Husayn, died 458 AH, investigation by Dr. 'Abd al-Mu'ti Qal'aji, Dar al-Kutub al-'Ilmiyya, Beirut, 1405 AH.
75. Radd al-Muhtar (Hashiyat Ibn 'Abidin) by Ibn 'Abidin Muhammad Amin, died 1252 AH, al-Babi al-Halabi, 2nd edition 1386/2 AH + Damascus edition, investigation by Dr. Husam al-Din ibn Muhammad Salih Farfur and others, Dar al-Thaqafa, Damascus, 1421/1 AH.
76. Ruh al-Ma'ani fi Tafsir al-Qur'an wa al-Sab' al-Mathani, by al-Alusi Shihab al-Din Mahmud ibn 'Abd Allah, died 1270 AH, Dar Ihya' al-Turath al-'Arabi, Beirut, facsimile of the Maymaniyya edition.
77. Al-Rawd al-Murbi' Sharh Zad al-Mustaqni', by al-Bahuti Mansur ibn Yunus, died 1051 AH, Dar al-Kutub al-'Ilmiyya, Beirut, 1st edition 1408/9 AH.
78. Rawdat al-Talibin wa 'Umdat al-Muftin, by al-Nawawi Muhyi al-Din, died 676 AH, al-Maktab al-Islami, Beirut, 1st edition 1412/3 AH.
79. Al-Zuhd wa al-Raqa'iq, by 'Abd Allah ibn al-Mubarak, investigation by Habib al-Rahman al-A'zami, printed in India, 1385 AH.
80. Al-Zawa'id 'ala Sunan Ibn Majah, by al-Busiri Ahmad ibn Abi Bakr, died 840 AH, = Sunan Ibn Majah.
81. Al-Zawajir 'an Iqtiraf al-Kaba'ir, by Ibn Hajar al-Haytami Ahmad ibn Muhammad, died 974 AH, Dar al-Ma'rifa, Beirut, 1402 AH.
82. Subul al-Huda wa al-Rashad fi Sirat Khayr al-'Ibad (peace be upon him), by al-Salihi Muhammad ibn Yusuf, died 942 AH, Dar al-Kutub al-'Ilmiyya, 1st edition 1414/1 AH.
83. Al-Siraj al-Munir Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir (by al-Suyuti), by al-'Azizi 'Ali ibn Ahmad, died 1070 AH, Cairo.
84. Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj al-Muwaddih li Kulli Talib Muhtaj (Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri), by al-Haddadi Abu Bakr ibn 'Ali, died 800 AH, (manuscript).
85. Al-Si'aya fi Kashf Ma fi Sharh al-Wiqaya, by al-Lakhnawi Muhammad 'Abd al-Hayy, died 1304 AH, Lahore, Pakistan, 1396 AH.
86. Sunan Ibn Majah, by Muhammad ibn Yazid al-Qazwini, died 275 AH, investigation by Muhammad Fu'ad 'Abd al-Baqi.
87. Sunan Abi Dawud, by Sulayman ibn al-Ash'ath al-Sijistani, died 275 AH, investigation by Shaykh Muhammad 'Awwamah, Dar al-Minhaj Jeddah, 3rd edition 1431 AH.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is the bibliography of the critical edition of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyarah. It lists 19 classical sources (numbered 69 to 87) used by the editor for verification. The sources include Hanafi fiqh works, hadith collections, biography, tafsir, and commentaries on earlier texts. Notable works: Al-Durr al-Mukhtar and its super-commentary Radd al-Muhtar by Ibn 'Abidin (entry 72 and 75) are core Hanafi reference works. Also included are commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri itself: Khulasat al-Dala'il (entry 70) and Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj (entry 84, a manuscript). The list shows the range of sources from early to later Hanafi scholarship, as well as Shafi'i works like Rawdat al-Talibin. Each entry provides author, death date, publication details, and editor if applicable. The editor has arranged them in alphabetical order by Arabic title. This front matter is essential for establishing the scholarly basis of the critical edition.

Key Terms
تحقيق (tahqiq): Critical edition or scholarly verification of a classical text
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH)
رد المحتار (Radd al-Muhtar): Super-commentary (hashiya) on Al-Durr al-Mukhtar by Muhammad Amin Ibn 'Abidin (d. 1252 AH), the authoritative reference for later Hanafi fatwa.
خلاصة الدلائل (Khulasat al-Dala'il): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Razi 'Ali ibn Ahmad Makki (d. 598 AH)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A critical edition's bibliography is a map of the Hanafi scholarly tradition, from the matn to the later authoritative commentaries that inform fatwa.

Key Hanafi Sources in the Bibliography
Listing bibliographic references

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi fiqh sources listed in the bibliography and distinguish them from works of hadith, history, and biography.

Core Idea
Know Fath al-Qadir, al-‘Inayah, and Fatawa Qadi Khan – they are essential Hanafi references.

This bibliography lists works used to verify the text of al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah. Beyond its editorial purpose, it reveals the canonical Hanafi references a student should know. We will scan the list and highlight the most important Hanafi fiqh sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi fiqh works
Look for titles that are commentaries on al-Hidayah (e.g., Fath al-Qadir, al-‘Inayah) or collections of fatwa (e.g., Fatawa Qadi Khan). These are core Hanafi texts.
Fath al-Qadir by Ibn al-Humam and al-‘Inayah by al-Babarti are both commentaries on al-Hidayah.
2
Distinguish non-fiqh works
Note works of hadith (e.g., Gharib al-Hadith, al-‘Ilal al-Kabir), biography (e.g., al-Tabaqat al-Kubra), and history (e.g., al-‘Uqud al-Lu’lu’iyyah). These are reference works but not Hanafi fiqh sources.
Even hadith works are important for usul, but the focus here is on fiqh sources.
3
Catalogue the Hanafi fiqh entries
List the numbers: 120 (Umdat al-Ri'ayah), 121 (al-‘Inayah = Fath al-Qadir), 124 (Ghunyat Dhawi al-Ahkam), 125 (Fatawa Qadi Khan), 126 (Fath Bab al-‘Inayah), 128 (Fath al-Qadir).
Some entries appear multiple times or cross-referenced.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography (فهرس مصادر التحقيق) listing sources used by the editor or author of the current book. It includes works of Hadith, Fiqh, history, and biographies. Many are classical Hanafi references such as 'Fath al-Qadir' (شرح الهداية) by Ibn al-Humam, 'Al-'Inayah' by al-Babarti, and 'Fatawa Qadi Khan'. Hadith works like 'Gharib al-Hadith' by Abu 'Ubayd and al-Khattabi are cited. The list shows the scholarly depth behind the verification process. The entries include author names, death dates (ت), publication details, and editors. Some are manuscripts (مخطوط). The numbers (113-128) are likely the serial numbers in the index. The bibliography provides a valuable reference for students to locate the original sources cited in the commentary.

Key Terms
فهرس مصادر التحقيق (fihris masādir al-taḥqīq): An index of sources used for verification and critical editing of the text.
فتح القدير (Fatḥ al-Qadīr): A major commentary on al-Hidayah by Ibn al-Humam, a key Hanafi reference.
العناية (al-‘Ināyah): Commentary on al-Hidayah by al-Babarti, often printed with Fath al-Qadir.
فتاوى قاضي خان (Fatāwā Qāḍī Khān): Fatwa collection by Hasan ibn Mansur al-Uzjandi (Qadi Khan), a standard Hanafi reference.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Sources Behind a Hanafi Commentary
Bibliography of sources used in al-Jawhara al-Nayyira

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key Hanafi fiqh and hadith sources listed in the bibliography and explain their significance in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A commentary's bibliography reveals the school's methodology: core matn supported by hadith musnads and earlier commentaries.

This passage is the bibliography of sources used in 'al-Jawhara al-Nayyira', a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The list includes foundational Hanafi texts like Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, as well as major hadith collections such as Musnad Ahmad and Musnad Abi Hanifah. Understanding these sources helps you appreciate the depth and breadth of Hanafi scholarship and the hierarchy of texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base matn
Locate the entry that is the primary text being commented upon. Look for 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' and note its author and death date.
This is entry 159; it is the core of the commentary.
2
Categorize the sources
Group entries into categories: fiqh matn (e.g., Mukhtasar al-Tahawi), fiqh sharh (e.g., Maraqi al-Falah), hadith musnad (e.g., Musnad Ahmad), hadith musannaf (e.g., al-Musannaf by Ibn Abi Shaybah), and language works (e.g., al-Misbah al-Munir).
Each category serves a distinct purpose: matn for basic rulings, sharh for explanation, musnad for hadith evidence.
3
Note the chronological spread
Observe the death dates of authors, from early (e.g., Abu Hanifa d.150 AH) to later (e.g., al-Shurunbulali d.1069 AH). This shows the diachronic development of Hanafi thought.
Earlier sources are closer to the founding generations; later ones are consolidations.
4
Recognize authority levels
Identify which sources belong to zahir al-riwayah (e.g., Mukhtasar al-Quduri) and which are later commentaries or nawadir (rare transmissions). This helps assess the weight of a ruling.
The editor's notes in the commentary often clarify the mufta bihi position.
5
Reflect on the commentator's method
Consider why the commentator would cite hadith musnads alongside fiqh matns. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle of combining revealed evidence (naql) with legal reasoning (ra'y).
The presence of many musnads underscores that Hanafi fiqh is not based solely on opinion but on hadith.

Commentary
This passage is the bibliography (فهرس مصادر التحقيق) of the book 'الجوهرة النيرة شرح لمختصر القدوري'. It lists the classical Hanafi and hadith sources used by the commentator, arranged numerically from number 158 onward (continuing from previous pages). The list includes foundational Hanafi texts such as Mukhtasar al-Quduri (the base text) and Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, as well as major hadith collections like Musnad Ahmad, Musnad Abi Hanifah, and al-Mustadrak ‘ala al-Sahihayn. It also references works of fiqh and language. Each entry provides the author's name, death date, editor, publisher, and edition details. For students, this index demonstrates the scholarly apparatus behind the commentary and the breadth of sources the Hanafi school draws upon, including both mutun (core texts) and shuruh (commentaries). The presence of many musnads (hadith collections) shows the importance of hadith evidence in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational text in Hanafi fiqh by Abu al-Husayn Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH). It is the base matn that 'al-Jawhara al-Nayyira' comments upon.
مختصر الطحاوي (Mukhtasar al-Tahawi): Another early Hanafi mukhtasar by Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH), often cited in later commentaries.
مسند الإمام أبي حنيفة (Musnad al-Imam Abi Hanifah): A collection of hadith attributed to Abu Hanifa, compiled by later scholars, with a commentary by al-Sunbahli.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Understanding the Author's Introduction to al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah
Author introduces his commentary on al-Quduri's text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and purpose of al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah and explain its relationship to Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Core Idea
Al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah is a concise commentary designed for students with limited understanding.

Classical Hanafi texts often begin with an introduction (muqaddima) where the author states his purpose and methodology. This passage opens al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah, a commentary on the well-known Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Understanding such introductions helps situate the work within the Hanafi tradition and clarifies its intended audience.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and work
Note that the author is the commentator of al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah, and he names his commentary. The base text is Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri.
The author does not name himself in this passage but uses the first person.
2
Understand the structure of the introduction
The introduction begins with basmala and hamdala, followed by blessings on the Prophet and Companions, then a statement of purpose. This is a standard pattern in Islamic scholarly works.
The phrase 'قال الشيخ الإمام أبو الحسين رحمه الله تعالى' signals the start of the original matn.
3
Analyze the stated purpose
The author says he compiled this commentary with 'concise expressions and clear phrases' and 'clarified it for those with limited understanding'. This tells us the work is aimed at beginners or intermediates.
The title 'al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah' (The Luminous Jewel) reflects its value.
4
Connect to the Hanafi madhhab
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational Hanafi manual. Commentaries like this one are essential for transmitting and explaining the madhhab's rulings.
Many such commentaries exist; al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah is known for its clarity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
مقدمة المؤلف
الحمد لله، ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله، وما توفيقي إلا بالله والصلاة والسلام على رسول الله سيدنا محمد بن عبد الله، وعلى أنبياء الله وملائكة الله ورضي الله عن الصحابة أولياء الله، وعن التابعين لهم في دين الله.
وبعد :
فهذا شرح لـ «مختصر القُدُوري»، جمعته بألفاظ مختصرة، وعبارات ظاهرة، يشتمل على كثير من المعاني والمذاكرة، أوضحته لذوي الأفهام القاصرة، والهمم المتقاصرة، وسميته: (الجوهرة النيرة).
واستعنت في ذلك بمن له الحمد في الأولى والآخرة، سبحانه هو أهل التقوى وأهل المغفرة.
قال الشيخ الإمام أبو الحسين رحمه الله تعالى:
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Author's introduction. Praise be to Allah, and there is no power nor strength except with Allah, and my success is only with Allah. May blessings and peace be upon the Messenger of Allah, our master Muhammad ibn Abdullah, and upon the prophets of Allah and the angels of Allah. May Allah be pleased with the Companions, the friends of Allah, and the Followers who succeeded them in the religion of Allah. To proceed: This is a commentary on 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri,' which I have compiled with concise expressions and clear phrases, encompassing many meanings and discussions. I have clarified it for those with limited understanding and deficient aspirations. I have named it 'al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah.' And I sought help from Him to whom belongs all praise in this world and the Hereafter; glorified is He, He is the Lord of piety and forgiveness. Imam Abu al-Husayn (may Allah have mercy on him) said:
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to his commentary. He begins with the basmala and hamdala, then explains his purpose: to write a concise and clear commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. He names his work 'al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah' (The Luminous Jewel). He mentions he has made it easy for those with limited understanding. Finally, he transitions to quoting the original text of al-Quduri with 'قال الشيخ الإمام أبو الحسين رحمه الله تعالى', which is the customary way to begin citing the matn.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The base legal text by Imam Abi Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational Hanafi manual.
الجوهرة النيرة (al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah): The title of this commentary, meaning 'The Luminous Jewel'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The author wrote al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah as a concise, clear commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri for students with limited understanding.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Author's Introduction: Purpose and Structure in Hanafi Fiqh Works
Opening doxology and author's statement of purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of a classical Hanafi fiqh introduction and state the author's stated purpose.

Core Idea
A fiqh author's preface reveals his intent, audience, and method.

In this passage, the author of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah begins with the traditional Islamic opening phrases, then explains why he wrote this commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. This standard front matter provides insight into the scholarly context and intended readership. Understanding these elements helps you situate the work within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opening invocations
Look for the basmalah, hamdalah, and the formula 'لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله'. These are standard in Islamic texts and set the tone of reliance on Allah.
The basmalah is almost universal in Hanafi works.
2
Recognize the praise of the Prophet and Companions
The author sends blessings upon the Prophet, his family, prophets, angels, and asks for Allah's pleasure upon the Companions and Followers. This reflects the Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah creed.
3
Find the statement of purpose
After 'وبعد', the author states his goal: to write a concise, clear commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, aimed at students with limited abilities.
The phrase 'لذوي الأفهام القاصرة' indicates the target audience.
4
Identify the book's title
The author names his work 'الجوهرة النيرة' (The Luminous Jewel). This is a common practice to name one's commentary distinctively.
5
Note the author's acknowledgment of divine help
He ends by seeking help from Allah, praising Him as worthy of piety and forgiveness. This shows humility and reliance on divine assistance.
Such acknowledgments are typical in Hanafi prefaces.

Commentary
This is the author's preface. He opens with the basmalah and hamdalah, then praises the Prophet and the Companions. He states his purpose: to write a concise but clear commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, intended for students of modest ability. He names his work 'The Luminous Jewel' and acknowledges his reliance on Allah. This is a standard prefatory section common in Hanafi fiqh works.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A widely used Hanafi fiqh manual by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), covering core rulings with brief wording.
الجوهرة النيرة (Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah): The title of this commentary, meaning 'The Luminous Jewel', written by an unidentified Hanafi scholar.

Key Takeaway
The author's preface in a Hanafi fiqh work provides essential context about the work's purpose, audience, and approach, which helps readers better understand and apply the text.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Navigating the Table of Contents of Al-Jawhara al-Nayra
Table of contents listing structure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major chapters and subsections of Hanafi fiqh as organized in Al-Jawhara al-Nayra and locate the starting point for purification rulings.

Core Idea
The table of contents is a roadmap: the first chapter is purification, which is the prerequisite for prayer.

Before diving into the rulings, it is essential to understand the structure of the text. This lesson walks you through the table of contents of Al-Jawhara al-Nayra, a key Hanafi commentary on al-Quduri. By parsing the chapter headings, you will see how Hanafi fiqh is organized and where to find specific topics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the front matter
Look at the entries before the author's introduction: editor's preface, biography of the author, study of the book, comparative examples. These are introductory and not fiqh rulings.
These help understand the text's context but are not part of the fiqh content.
2
Locate the first fiqh chapter
The first chapter after the author's introduction is 'Kitab al-Taharah' (Book of Purification). This is always the starting point in Hanafi fiqh manuals.
Purification is a prerequisite for prayer (salah).
3
Examine the subsections of Taharah
The TOC lists: Obligatory acts of wudu, sunnah acts, nullifiers, ghusl obligations, types, sunnah, causes of ghusl, water rulings, wells, captives, tayammum, wiping over khuffs. These are the main topics covered under purification.
Each subsection corresponds to a section in the book.
4
Note the sequence of topics
Observe the order: wudu details first, then ghusl, then water, then tayammum, then khuffs. This sequence reflects the logical progression from lesser to greater purification and from common to special cases.
Understanding this order helps in later study.

Source Text

نماذج ونصوص مقارنة من السراج الوهاج والجوهرة النيرة
١ - مسألة حكم دفع الزوج زكاته إلى زوجته وبالعكس.
٢- مسألة القيام من الركوع في صفة الصلاة.

Biography of the author of al-Jawhara al-Nayra: his name, lineage, birth; his pursuit of knowledge, mention of his teachers; his students; praise of scholars for him and mention of his good fragrant life; his works; his death, may Allah have mercy on him; description of his works. Study of al-Jawhara with explanation of the author's methodology in it, and mention of its status and merits. Merits of the book al-Jawhara al-Nayra. Comparative examples and texts from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawhara al-Nayra: 1. Issue of the ruling of a husband giving his zakat to his wife and vice versa; 2. Issue of standing from bowing in the description of prayer; 3. Issue of condition of the Imam's permission for reviving dead land. Sources of the author in al-Jawhara al-Nayra. Commentary
This passage is a detailed table of contents from the critical edition of al-Jawhara al-Nayra, a Hanafi commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It lists the front matter, including the editor's introduction, biography of the author (Mulla Akhyar?), a study of the book, comparative examples, and then the chapter headings. The chapters begin with Kitab al-Taharah (Purification) covering wudu, ghusl, water, wells, captives, tayammum, and wiping over khuffs. The list shows the structure of the book, which is a systematic exposition of Hanafi fiqh according to the matn of al-Quduri.

Key Terms
الطهارة (al-taharah): The chapter on purification, the first major section of fiqh.
الوضوء (al-wudu): Ablution with water; the obligatory and sunnah acts are listed.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Structure of Hanafi Fiqh in Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyira
Table of contents of Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyira

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major sections and chapters of Hanafi fiqh as arranged in Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyira, and explain how the table of contents reflects the madhhab's systematic approach to purification and prayer.

Core Idea
Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyira systematically covers Hanafi fiqh from purification to prayer, with detailed sub-sections.

This lesson introduces the table of contents of Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyira, a classical Hanafi commentary on Mukhtasar Al-Quduri. The table of contents is not just a list but a map of the Hanafi fiqh curriculum, starting with the fundamentals of purification (ṭahārah) and moving to prayer (ṣalāh). Understanding this structure helps you appreciate how the Hanafi school organizes its legal rulings practically and pedagogically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main books
Look at the table of contents: it begins with 'The Book of Purification' (كتاب الطهارة) and then 'The Book of Prayer' (كتاب الصلاة). These are the foundational sections of Hanafi fiqh that Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyira covers.
Other books like fasting, zakat, etc., are not included; the commentary focuses on these two initially.
2
Examine the sub-sections of Purification
Under Purification, notice the progression: obligations of wudu, sunan, nullifiers, then ghusl, tayammum, wiping over socks, menstruation, etc. This order reflects the typical Hanafi sequence from minor to major purification.
Each sub-section addresses a specific legal aspect, e.g., 'Nullifiers of wudu' follows 'Obligations' because one must know what breaks purity.
3
Examine the sub-sections of Prayer
Under Prayer, the list covers times, adhan, conditions, description, differences for women, recitation, and congregation. This shows the Hanafi emphasis on practical details.
The inclusion of 'woman differs from man in ten places' highlights the gender-specific rulings.
4
Note the editorial front matter
Before the content, the table lists manuscript copies, editions, biographies, and indices. These are tools for scholars to verify the text.
This is typical of critical editions; it shows the book's scholarly apparatus.
5
Relate to the Hanafi madhhab
The structure reflects the Hanafi tradition: rulings are grouped by ibādāt (acts of worship) in a logical sequence. This organization helps students build knowledge step by step.
Other madhhabs might arrange topics differently, but this sequence is characteristic of Hanafi fiqh works.

Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents (فهرس الموضوعات) of the book Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyira, a Hanafi fiqh commentary on Mukhtasar Al-Quduri. It lists the main sections and chapters covered in the work, beginning with the author's introduction, then the Book of Purification (كتاب الطهارة) with detailed sub-sections on ablution, ritual bath, water, Tayammum, wiping over socks, menstruation, and impurity. It then moves to the Book of Prayer (كتاب الصلاة) covering times, adhan, conditions, description, differences for women, recitation, and congregation. This table of contents provides a structured overview of the fiqh topics systematically arranged according to the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
الطهارة (al-ṭahārah): The Book of Purification, a main section in Hanafi fiqh covering physical and ritual cleanliness.
الصلاة (al-ṣalāh): The Book of Prayer, a main section covering obligatory and voluntary prayers, conditions, and descriptions.
وضوء (wudū’): Ablution, the minor ritual purification using water on specific body parts.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is listed as a sub-section under the Book of Prayer in the table of contents?
A) Nullifiers of Tayammum
B) Obligations of ritual bath
C) Congregational prayer
D) Purification of wells

Key Takeaway
Al-Jawhara Al-Nayyira's table of contents reveals the Hanafi pedagogical sequence: purification before prayer, with detailed sub-categories reflecting the madhhab's systematic approach to fiqh.
